And could those flames some lovely maid destroy,
A nation's glory and a parent's joy?
Could babes, sweet-smiling, claim no hand to save,
But find, unwept, a furnace for a grave?
Thus mourned his generous heart the doom severe,
And paid lost Ai the tribute of a tear.
Like ocean's long, deep roar, a rushing sound
Burst from the wood, and poured along the ground;
At once wide trembled over the awful fields
The sudden gleam of spears, and helms, and shields,
Impetuous rolled unseen the rattling car,
And banner'd terrors waved the approach of war.
Loud rung bold Irad's voice; the dreadful sound
Stopped the long host, and s^ook the affrighted ground;
Thrice, like the burst of thunder, hoarse he cried;
Thrice, stood the host; and thrice the sky (...).
The cry waved solemn through the winding vales;
Night shook, and murmurs filled the rushing gales.
The southern guards soon caught the boding sound,
And spread the alarm the startled camp around;
Loud as tall billows rend the rocky shore,
Rose the sonorous clarion's bursting roar:
Swift to the camp the hero winged his way,
Roused all the host, and scattered wild dismay --
Arm, warriors, arm! to instant battle fly!
The foe's at hand! ye combat, or ye die.
Swift to these tents unnumber'd bands repair;
Hark! how the trumpet fills the troubled air!
In southern fields ascends the wasting war,
And fierce as whirlwinds rolls the rapid car.
Arm, ere our camp be wrapped in one broad flame,
And Israel's manly thousands want a name,
Thus, round the host, his animating cry
Urged sleep's oblivious hand from every eye;
Each waking mind the strange alarm appalls;
Arm, warriors, arm! each startled hero calls:
From tent to tent the wild confusion flies;
Shouts rend the plains; groans murmur; shrieks arise;
A rushing noise invades the listening ear;
In swift succession half-seen forms appear;
Shrill rings the rattling mail; the trump's big sound
Cleaves the dun heaven, and shakes the gloomy ground.
Round a broad flame, that, by the Chief's command,
Shoots lofty spires, and gleams along the sand,
Deep throng the squadrons; high the standards stream,
And wave, and glimmer, in the livid beam.
There, while the terrors of the lovely fair
Froze every breast, and breathed a wide despair,
A quickening glow the Leader's voice inspired;
Hushed were their cries; their lessening fears retired;
Through every bosom thrilled a new delight,
And braced each sinew for the manly sight.
Now, ranged in ranks, the host expectant stood,
Prepared for combat, steeled to death and blood;
Sudden, before the Chief, with panting breast,
The generous Youth preferred his bold request --
Near Ai's red flames I steered my careless way,
Robbed of wished slumbers, and to grief a prey,
When sheathed in gleaming arms, a mighty train,
Poured from the wood, and covered all the plain:
On foaming coursers, chiefs impel the war,
Or whirl the terrors of the wasting car.
And will thou, Chief divine, from Irad hear
The dictates of a mind, that knows no fear?
Shall this young arm again the lance command,
And lead to fight a strong, undaunted band,
To Ai's wide ruins wing our active course,
And tempt the fury of barbarian force?
Shall thine unconquered sword the camp defend,
And ward the fate, if shame our steps attend?
Safe in thy prudence shall the race endure,
And Joshua's name our wives, and sons secure.
Lo, dressed in steel, we wait thy ruling breath!
Counsel is ruin, and delay is death.
Go, in JEHOVAH's name -- the Chief replied --
Forth stalked the Youth, and warmed with martial pride;
Over southern fields the bands appointed steered,
Squared in just ranks, and not a warrior feared.
Now where Ai's sons bestrew'd the plain, they came,
Faintly illumined by the distant flame;
No foe appeared: the world more gloomy grew,
And, lost in clouds, etherial realms withdrew;
Save where lone stars diffused a feeble beam,
Like the far taper's solitary gleam:
Slow winds breathed hollow through the dark profound,
And deepening horror brooded over the ground.
East of proud Ai, an ancient forest stood,
And southward far was stretched the lofty wood;
North lay fair plains; and next the walls, arrayed
With scattered trees, a spacious level spread.
Now near the burning domes, the squadrons stood,
Their breasts impatient for the scenes of blood:
On every face a death-like glimmer sat,
The unblessed harbinger of instant fate.
High through the gloom, in pale and dreadful spires,
Rose the long terrors of the dark-red fires;
Torches, and torrent sparks, by whirlwinds driven,
Streamed through the smoke, and fired the clouded heaven.
As often tall turrets sunk with rushing sound,
Broad flames burst forth, and sweep the etherial round,
The bright expansion lightened all the scene,
And deeper shadows lengthened over the green.
Loud through the walls that cast a golden gleam,
Crowned with tall pyramids of bending flame,
As thunders rumble down the dardening vales,
Rolled the deep solemn voice of rushing gales:
The bands admiring gazed the wondrous fight,
And Expectation trembled for the fight.
At once the sounding clarion breathed alarms;
Wide from the forest burst the flash of arms;
Thick gleam'd the helms; and over astonished fields,
Like thousand meteors, rose the flame-bright shields.
In gloomy pomp, to furious combat rolled
Ranks sheathed in mail, and chiefs in glimmering gold;
In floating lu^^re bounds the dim-seen steed,
And cars unfinished, swift to cars succeed:
From all the host ascends a dark-red glare,
Here in full blaze, in distant twinklings there;
Slow waves the dreadful light, as round the shore
Night's solemn blasts with deep concussion roar,
So rushed the footsteps of the embattled train,
And send an awful murmur over the plain.
Tall in the opposing van, bold Irad stood,
And bid the clarion sound the voice of blood.
Loud blew the trumpet on the sweeping gales,
Rocked the deep groves, and echoed round the vales;
A ceaseless murmur all the concave fills,
Waves through the quivering camp, and trembles over the hills.
High in the gloomy blaze the standards flew;
The impatient Youth his burnished falchion drew;
Ten-thousand swords his eager bands displayed,
And crimson terrors danced on every blade.
With equal rage, the bold, Hazorian train
Poured a wide deluge over the shadowy plain;
Loud rose the songs of war, loud clang'd the shields,
Dread shouts of vengeance shook the shuddering fields;
With mingled din, shrill, martial music rings,
And swift to combat each fierce hero springs.
So broad, and dark, a midnight storm ascends,
Bursts on the main, and trembling nature rends;
The red foam burns, the watery mountains rise,
One deep unmeasured thunder heaves the skies;
The bark drives lonely; shivering and forlorn,
The poor, sad sailors wish the lingering morn:
Not with less fury rushed the vengeful train;
Not with less tumult roared the embattled plain.
Now in the oak's black shade they fought concealed*
And now they shouted through the open field;
The long, pale splendors of the curling flame
Cast over their polished arms a livid gleam;
An umber'd luster floated round their way,
And lighted falchions to the fierce affray.
Now the swift chariots against the stubborn oak
Dashed; the dark earth re-echoes to the shock.
From shade to shade the forms tremendous stream,
And their arms flash a momentary flame.
Mid hollow tombs, as fleets an airy train,
Lost in the skies, or fading over the plain;
So visionary shapes, around the fight,
Shoot through the gloom, and vanished from the sight;
Through twilight paths the maddening coursers bound,
The shrill swords crack, the clashing shields resound.
There, lost in grandeur might the eye behold
The dark-red glimmerings of the steel, and gold;
The chief; the steed; the nimbly-rushing car;
And all the horrors of the gloomy war.
Here the thick clouds, with purple luster bright,
Spread over the long long host and gradual sunk in night;
Here half the world was wrapped in rolling fires,
And dreadful valleys sunk between the spires.
Swift ran black forms across the livid flame,
And oaks waved slowly in the trembling beam:
Loud rose the mingled noise; with hollow sound,
Deep-rolling whirlwinds roar, and thundering flames resound.
As drives a blast along the midnight heath,
Rushed raging Irad on the scenes of death;
High over his shoulder gleam'd his brandished blade,
And scattered ruin round the twilight shade.
Full on a giant hero's sweeping car
He poured the tempest of resistless war;
His twinkling lance the heathen raised on high,
And hurled it, fruitless, through the gloomy sky;
From the bold Youth the maddening coursers wheel,
Gash'd by the vengeance of his slaughtering steel,
'Twixt two tall oaks the helpless chief they drew;
The shrill car dashed; the cracked wheels rattling flew;
Crushed in his arms, to rise he strove in vain,
And lay unpitied on the dreary plain.
Now Samlah's hands to war the chariot guide,
^air, beauteous, tall, famed Hamor's youngest pride;
Over Achsaph's towers he stretched a potent sway,
And saw surrounding realms his rod obey.
Adnor* an elder birth, proud grandeur spurned;
Lord of his soul, inferior realms he scorned;
Nor felt one pang, nor showed one envious frown,
When doting Age to Sam^ah gave the crown.
Round his young steps he cast a kind survey,
And taught the blessings of an equal sway;
The pride of arts a^lur'd him to pursue;
To wisdom formed him, and to virtue drew;
To reason's rules his stormy passions wrought,
And shone, a pattern of the truths he taught.
From Jabin's loins a matchless virgin sprung,
And every voice with Salma's praises rung.
Her, Adnor led to share his brother's throne,
And made, delighted, Samlah's bliss his own.
Five weeks the prince beheld in transport glide,
Blessed in the beauties of his lovely bride:
Heedless of war he dwelt, 'till Jabin's voice
Roused him to arms, and called to ruder joys.
Now, where bold Irad scattered blood and fate,
In the same car the friendly brothers ^ate;
When Adnor thus -- Oh fly yon miscreant's arm;
Nor tempt the terrors of the sweeping storm!
Its wonted aid my broken spear denies --
With a fierce look, the impatient youth replies --
Me do thou urge to base, unmanly flight?
Leap from the chariot; hide in covering night?
Shall Salma hear? shall Samlah's growing name
Waste with the pangs of never-ending shame?
He said, and furious, urged his rapid car,
Crushed the firm ranks, and shouted to the war;
On Irad's course he drove; the hero turned,
And a brown glimmering from his buckler burned:
'Twixt the bold leaders poured an ardent band;
Sword clash'd on sword, and hand rose up to hand;
They fell; new squadrons over their corses rise,
And louder tumults echo from the skies.
Imperious Samlah lifts a haughty cry --
Hence, on your lives, presuming dallards fly*
Who dares transgress shall find a sudden doom:
Give Samlah place -- give kings, and heroes room --
He spoke. His friends, all anxious for their king,
Still crowd the war, and swift to danger spring;
Loud sung the vengeance of his pointed steel,
And a bold veteran, deeply wounded, fell;
Enraged, the bands on either side retreat,
And leave the furious monarch to his fate.
Swift from the chariot faithful Adnor sprang;
On Irad's shield his rushing falchion rang:
The Youth's quick wheeling, through his shoulder glides;
Drops the cleft arm, and gush the living tides.
He sunk; and Irad, touched with pity, cried --
Ah youth! whose bosom glows with generous pride,
To scenes of endless gloom thy spirit flies;
Wing, wing thy voice, for pardon, to the skies!
Oh, Sire of all, may this brave warrior's mind,
In life's fair climes, some lowly mansion find!
He spoke. The chief his answering mind addressed --
If soft compassion warm thy friendly breast,
Oh hear! nor spurn a dying brother's prayer!
Let Samlah's tender years thy pity share!
Oh may a sire, a bride, thy bosom move!
The charms of beauty, and the calls of love!
Thus the kind youth, and fainting, as he cried,
He lived for Samlah, and for Samlah died.
So frowned dread night on Abraham's fatal plain,
When thou, Montgomery, pride of chiefs, wast slain.
Spare, sons of freedom! spare that generous tear;
To heaven resign, nor name the doom severe --
Great, brave, and just, to ward Columbia's shame,
He hunted toil, in fields of growing fame;
Alive, fair Victory never forsook his side;
He lived in triumph, and in glory died.
Still bards shall sing, to earth's remotest clime,
He bled for all, and every heart for him.
Glued to his side, to untimely fate a prey,
There bright Macpherson breathed his life away.
Round the fair youth in vain soft graces glowed,
And science charmed him to her sweet abode;
In vain fond parents hoped his steps again,
And worth approved, and realms admired, in vain.
Yet patriot virtue writes the glory high,
With such a chief, in such a cause, to die.
Soft spoke the chief -- O youth! thy virtuous bloom.
Asked a lot milder, and a later tomb.
Is there no blissful seat, by Heaven assigned
To the fair efforts of a clouded mind?
To life well-acted, can no grace supply
A sweet remission, and a happy sky?
But thou, base coward, claim'st the avenging sword;
Could thou look on, and see thy brother gored?
That best of brothers, whose concluding breath
Restrains the falchion, and delays thy death?
Pale Samlah heard, and over the embodied wall
He rushed, regardless of his brother's fall,
From rank to rank with panting breast he flew,
Where the war opened, and the coursers drew;
Behind, fierce Irad drove his dreadful way,
And left at distance far the pallid ray;
Ten thousand spears around him pierce the gloom;
Ten thousand warriors rush to hastening doom;
Through the black either smoky volumes flow,
And with brown light their skirts all-umber'd glow;
Far over conflicting trains the sheets descend;
The deep night thickens* and the shades extend.
There Uzal brave a stubborn fight maintained,
And crowned with matchless strength, retreat disdained;
Dan's mighty chief -- On Ai's inglorious plain,
When vanquished Israel left their kindred slain,
His stiff, strong buckler braved the fierce affray,
Sheltered the flight, and covered all the way.
Now, in the center, shrill his armor rung,
Where the darts shower'd, and where the javelins sung,
But still his dauntless footsteps onward drove;
Nor thronged battalions could those footsteps move.
On all sides round, a thousand twilight forms
Invade the war, and strike their ringing arms;
Here, against the chief, prepared to pierce his foe,
The lance unheeded aimed the fatal blow;
There, whilst the warrior listened to the alarm,
High over his helmet hung the uplifted arm.
Unnumber'd bucklers twinkle round the field,
In light now dreadful, now in shades concealed.
Still more remote, involved in deeper gloom,
Where hands unnotic'd dealt the frequent doom,
Shelumiel fought; the prince of Simeon's trains,
Famed in the contests of a thousand plains.
Meantime, dark Hazor's sons to battle rolled,
And vast Madonians, wrapped in barbarous gold:
These, with their leaders, near the dreadful ray,
Whirled the swift car, and drove their rapid way.
There, dressed in gold, tremendous Jabin shone,
And winged the terrors of his moving throne.
He Hazor's realms with mighty scepter swayed,
And his proud nod unnumber'd hosts obeyed.
A genius vast, with cool attention joined,
To wisdom fashioned his superior mind:
No scene unnotic'd 'scap'd his searching view;
The arts of peace, and arts of war, he knew;
To no kind wish, or tender tear, a prey;
But taught by keen discernment equal sway:
Interest, of all his life the unshaken guide,
Unmoved by passion, and unmoved by pride.
He first, inventive, to the waste of war
Led the tall steed, and drove the dreadful car.
To arms, beneath the standard, veterans trained,
And every movement, every f^int, explained:
Close, lest his conduct watchful chiefs should arm;
Slow to decide, and vigorous to perform:
With firm, fierce bravery forced his foes to fly,
And gave one law -- to conquer, or to die.
Now his great mind, by long successes fired,
To matchless fame, and single rule, aspired;
In the same cause, beneath his banner joined,
His voice, his art, this countless host combined,
In night's concealing hour, prepared the affray,
And promised triumph, ere the dawning ray.
High in his flame-bright car his spear he raised;
A crimson glory from his armor blazed;
Conquer, he cried, or fall, ye dauntless bands,
The noblest heroes of a thousand lands.
Shall this brave host to Israel yield the night?
Few in their numbers; timorous in the fight --
Shall we, inglorious, blot our ancient fame?
Forbid it virtue, and forbid it shame.
Lo here the man, ye chose to guide your path,
Prepared for glory, or prepared for death;
This arm shall guide you through the dastard band;
First in the fight, as first in sway, I stand.
He spoke, and fiercely winged his rapid car;
As fierce the squadrons rush to glorious war;
All dropped the javelin* all the falchion wheeled;
A copious slaughter drenched the glimmering field;
From their dire arms a fearful splendour came,
And over their faces waved the gloomy flame.
Hand joined to hand, the vengeful thousands raged;
Man challenged man, and sword with sword engaged;
The victors rushed; (...) pierced in anguish cried*
No flight; no fear they conquered, or they died;
For Israel's dauntle^s sons maintained the field,
And chief with chief the dread assault repelled;
Round the wild region mingled horrors reigned;
Nor those would yield, nor these the victory gained.
First, in the van, imperious Jabin's car
Bore down whole tro^ps, and broke the thickening war.
High over the rest his dreadful voice was heard;
High over the rest his lofty form appeared;
His shield a crimson moon, before him spread,
And over his visage hovering horrors played;
His steeds, like rapid winds, impatient flew;
His sword the first, his spear the distant, slew;
Round the dark chariot countless weapons hung,
And groans, with sullen murmur, ceaseless rung;
Rank after rank he turned to hated ^light,
And joyful Hazor thronged the stubborn sight.
Before this dreadful path, two heroes sought,
And warmed with vengeance, countless wonders wrought.
Sons of one sire, that in the desert fell,
When impious Korah bade the host rebel.
The helpless orphans generous Caleb bred,
In arms instructed, and to combat led.
With mutual flame their friendly bosoms loved;
In peace together lived, in war together moved.
Now, side to side, the manly heroes stood,
And sable torrents from their falchions flowed;
When Shammah thus -- thou best of friends, behold
Yon heathen's car, in gloomy terror rolled.
How his fierce coursers wing their rapid way!
How his keen falchion cleaves the yielding prey!
Say, shall our force the mighty Chief defy,
His arm experience, and his falchion try?
Or death, or triumph, shall the deed await;
And what is death, in Israel's dubious fate?
To prove fierce danger for his maker's laws,
And proffer life to save his country's cause,
Thou know, brave chief, Seraiah quick replied --
The good man's duty, and the brave man's pride.
He spoke* and fiercely plunging through the war,
Hewed a wide path, and burst upon the car,
Nor Shammah stayed. On Jabin's spacious shield
His rapid lance Seraiah's hand impelled;
Through the thick orb the point no passage found,
Its shade dark-quivering in the flamy round.
With a short flash, across the thickening air
The furious Heathen drove the greedy spear;
Swift on Seraiah's helmet sunk the steel;
His red arms rang; the hero groaned and fell.
With pangs, bold Shammah saw his brother's doom,
And wheeled his fiery falchion through the gloom;
From Jabin's hand a second javelin sped,
Sung through his ear, and pierced his gushing head;
Shrill rose the conqueror's shout; and all around
The plains remurmur, and the woods resound.
Now, more remote from Ai's decreasing light,
Slow moved a giant to the dreadful fight.
As when dun smoke, over all the horizon spread,
Pours round the setting moon a crimson shade,
Distained with blood, her broad, and dreadful eye
Looks death, and ruin, from the shuddering sky,
So gleams the circuit of his flame-bright shield,
And casts wide terror through the quaking field,
A beam-like spear commands his horrid way,
And all, before him, shun the dire affray.
And now fierce Israel's sons, with sad surprise,
To find brave Irad turned their boding eyes.
Far round they gazed; his form no more appeared;
They listened; but his voice no more was heard.
Then every bosom sudden fears appall;
Their nerves all stiffen, and their falchions fall;
A timorous fight their frozen hands sustain,
And sighs, and backward looks, confess their pain.
With shouts of triumph, swift the Heathens rolled,
And a bright terror flashed from flamy gold;
A thousand moony shields before them burned;
Ranks fell at once, and troops to flight were turned;
Each fatal step increased the piles of slain,
And boundless ruin ravaged all the plain.
As when a storm in midnight pomp extends,
And a broad deluge on the world descends,
From steep to steep, disdaining every goal,
Swelled with hoarse thunders, mountain-torrents roll;
The vales all echo to the dreadful sound;
The torn rocks roar; the cracking trees resound.
Meantime bold Irad far had crossed the fight,
And Samlah vanished with auspicious flight;
Round the dread region gazed the Youth serene,
And eyed the grandeur of the solemn scene.
Unnumber'd phantoms crowd the dusky war;
The half-seen hero, and unfinished car:
Black were the shades, as midnight in the tomb,
And floating glimmerings spread a fearful gloom.
Now rolled the distant cries an awful sound;
Now nearer clamors shook the embattled ground.
At once, from western fields, a shout ascends;
The plains all tremble, and the concave rends:
Quick turned the chief, while sad alarms inspire,
And saw dark forms, that passed along the fire;
Slow towered the camp the shouting squadrons move,
And long pale spires tremendous wave above.
Ah wretch! he cried -- to childish heat a prey!
How soon wild passion drove my steps astray!
What chief, less vain, shall lay the increasing fear?
Who cheer the bands, my presence ought to cheer?
Ah! should disgrace, and dire defeat, ensue,
No more this guilty face shall Joshua view;
These eyes never open on a host undone,
But death, or glory, by this arm be won.
Thus as he spoke, he crossed the deep array;
To his known form they yield an easy way:
Red flash his arms; and high above the field,
Gleams the drear luster of his orbed shield.
So, pale, and dreadful, through the midnight shade,
Sails a broad meteor over the mountain's head:
Dim rise the cliffs; and on the kindling air,
Stream the long terrors of its sanguine hair.
His voice resounding through the gloomy fight,
Revived their strength, and turned the increasing flight.
Fly, dastards, fly; desert your Maker's laws;
Your name dishonor; yield your country's cause;
But come, ye friends of Israel's injured name,
Sons of the skies, and heirs of deathless fame!
Know, round the distant plains, by chiefs inspired,
By virtue prompted, and by vengeance fired,
Bold, manly warriors, never taught to yield,
Cleave their fell foes, and sweep the dusty field;
Let this bright pattern every breast inflame;
Here lift your swords, where Irad leads to fame.
Thus every rank his voice invites to arms;
His presence actuates; his example charms;
From band to band, with nimble course, he flies,
Wheels the long host, and wakes intenser cries;
Thick flash the falchions; thick the javelins rain;
And shooting banners tremble over the plain;
In every scene, alert, the youth appears;
Each chief, each rank, his cry with transport hears;
Shouts fiercely bursting listening earth appall,
And hovering Conquest yet suspends her fall.
And now bold Irad, through the thickest war,
Drove the tall chief, and darkly rolling car,
When, lo! the giant full before him stood,
Involved in death, and covered over with blood:
Like some vast wave, approached the horrid form,
Heedless of spears, and raptured with the storm.
His wondrous size the admiring Youth beheld,
And snatched a lance that glittered on the field;
Loud rang the weapon on the monster's brow;
Backward he quick recoiled, and bending low,
Stood staggering. Irad waved his dreadful sword,
Springing impetuous; swift between them poured
Two gloomy chariots, of their lords despoiled,
And fierce around them thousand heroes toiled:
No more the chief could find his destined prey,
But turned, and mingled in the fierce affray.
Now loud, and solemn, through the roaring vales
Swelled the hoarse murmurs of the sounding gales,
With deep confusion shook the cliff's tall brow,
And rushed tempestuous on the world below;
From grove to grove the blast impatient flies,
Rends the stiff oak, and howls along the skies,
On Ai's broad flames, with wild dominion, falls,
And pours ten thousand thunders round her walls.
More wide, more b^ight, the folding fires ascend,
Heave the dun smoke, and far in either bend;
The glittering brands, by rapid whirlwinds driven,
Stream, like dim meteors, over the blackened heaven;
Swift through the woods red paths expanding roll;
Long heavy volumes thicken round the pole;
From all the concave sparks in torrents rain,
And fiery tempests rush along the plain.
Far through the groves the furious flames had spread,
And thousand fires rose scattered in the shade,
Ere Hazor's bands (so eager raged the fight)
Beheld, wi^h sad amaze, the fearful sight.
Then Jabin's voice, terrific, bade retire,
And the g^ad warriors sled the widening fire.
Israel pursued; but Jab^n's deathful arm
Whole troops repelled, and braved the wasting storm:
With the fierce giant, over the rear he rose,
And cooled the vengeance of his ardent foes,
Then to the sight, that still, with dreadful sway,
Rent eastern plains, brave Irad winged his way.
Part of the foes, that in the wood remained,
Had fled the heat, and safe recesses gained;
Part, lodged in open fields, maintained the war,
And sho^ts rebe^^ow'd to^e the murmuring air.
Sudden, over all the bands, resounds a cry --
Fled are our friends; we conquer, or we die:
Lo round the wood the kindling torrents burn;
Fix here our ranks; no warrior can return --
Then fierce despair the dauntless bosom fired,
Winged the keen falchion, and the arm inspired;
The chiefs exhorted, threatened, shouted, cried;
The ranks rushed onward, met the steel, and died;
For Israel's sons a moveless fight maintain,
Glued to the field, and cleaving man to man;
Brave Irad's dreadful voice the heroes armed,
Strung every nerve, and every weapon warmed;
On friend, and foe, alike the blind sword fell;
And the son sunk beneath the parent's steel.
Wild, and more wild, the ruin raged around;
Shouts rung; groans murmured; thunders rocked the ground;
Through the rent concave rushed the loud acclaim,
Swelled with the roaring wind, and fierce resounding flame,
At length a heathen's voice -- Retire, retire,
Where yon black opening parts the raging fire --
Quick, at the sound, along the glimmering shade,
Through the wide forest panting heroes fled,
In different courses, where the moory ground
Cleft the deep blaze, and formed a verdant mound.
Swift as the rapid blast, the youthful train
Nimbly precipitated over the plain;
On every side, the flames, with wild career,
Roared near their path, and added wings to fear;
None turned a gazing eye; but, with blessed flight,
Streamed through the grove, and escaped the vengeful light.
Behind, his path pale age more slow dragged on*
And wished, in vain, impending fate to shun;
Now here, now there, with feeble steps, they turned;
And here, and there, the fire terrific burned.
From tree to tree it flew; and all around
The moulder'd pines, with hoarsely rushing sound,
Fell thundering. Kindled ruins hedged their path;
Behind them swift pursued the blazing death;
Before, beside, and bending over their head,
The bright, and scorching splendors fiercely played;
Weak, and more weak, the cries of anguish came,
Drowned in the roaring fury of the flame.
To the dire forest Israel's sons pursued,
And heathen blood their reeking swords imbrued;
Then by the chief's command returned from fight,
The attentive squadrons eyed the wondrous sight,
Far sound the dreadful region, trees on high,
Wave their tall blazing summits in the sky;
Through the dark air, in crimson terror, sail
Broad sheets of flame, and bend along the gale;
Loud, and more loud, the raging whirlwind pours;
From wood to wood the rushing deluge roars;
Then, up vast eastern hills with fury driven,
Rolls over aerial cliffs, and kindles heaven:
The mountain groves, a long, long ridge of fire,
Shoot their tall flames, and through the clouds aspire.
Over dim-seen rocks, brown plains, and glimmering streams
Floats the pale luster of the trembling beams;
The camp astonished casts a quivering gaze,
And distant towns are lost in dumb amaze:
Retired the squadrons, range in dread array,
And watch the splendors of approaching day. --
THE CONQUEST OF CANAAN. BOOK VIII.

ARGUMENT.
Morning. Joshua joins Irad. Jobab's character, and challenge. Irad accepts it,
and kills Jobab. Battle. Irad kills Samlah, and engages Jabin. His death. Judah
routed with great slaughter. Death of Uzal, and Shelumiel. Caleb* with a large
division, marches out, rallies Judah, and renews the battle. Irad's death
throws the whole army into confusion. Joshua inspirits them, and makes great
havoc of the enemy. Zimri's exploits. He kills the king of the Hittites, and
routs them. Joshua kills the king of Shimron, and routs the center. Jabin,
perceiving the other divisions of the army defeated, orders a retreat, which is
performed with regularity. Joshua's lamentation over Irad. Scene of Selima's
distress at the sight of his corpse. Evening.

THE CONQUEST OF CANAAN. BOOK VIII.
OVER misty hills the day star led the morn,
And streaming light in heaven began to burn;
Wide scenes of woe the boundless blaze displayed,
Where the steel triumphed, and the deluge spread.
On wasted plains unnumber'd corses lay,
And smokes far scattered climbed upon the day,
Still clouded flames over eastern mountains rise,
And Ai's broad ruins sadden all the skies.
When lo! in glimmering arms, and black array,
Like storms low-hovering in the etheriatl way,
Far round the north a gloomy cloud ascends,
Its horror deepens, and its breadth extends.
Compact and firm, as moved by one great soul,
A front immense, the widening squadrons roll;
Thick shoot the spears; the trembling helmets beam,
And waving bucklers cast a moony gleam.
As the dire comet, swift through either driven,
In solemn silence climbs the western heaven;
His sanguine hair, portending fearful wars,
Streams down the midnight sky, and blots the stars;
Pale death and terror light the dusky gloom,
And quivering nations read their sudden doom.
So in the flaming van great Joshua rose,
And shot red glories on the wondering foes.
At his command the trumpet sounded high,
Aerial ensigns dancing in the sky;
Near and more near, they traced a dreadful way,
Joined Irad's host, and stretched in long array.
From Hazor's ranks that now before the wood,
In three embattled squares, refulgent stood,
Great Jobab strode. In Madon's realms he reigned:
Red was his eye, his brow with blood distained;
A beam his spear; his vast, expanded shield
Shot a bright morning over the crimson field;
His head sublime a mighty helmet crowned;
His quivering plumes with sable horror frowned;
Six cubits from the earth, he raised his frame;
His wish was battle, and his life was fame.
Proud was his father, prouder was the son:
Naught moved his pride; the tear, nor piercing groan:
Unmatched his force, he claimed a matchless fame,
And every combat decked his brightening name.
Princes, his captived slaves, before him bowed,
Stalked in his train, and round his chariot rode;
While their fair partners, first in triumph led,
Held the rich cup, or graced the brutal bed.
Often had surrounding realms his aid required,
Ere Zimri's hand Ai's hapless turrets fired;
But still their prayers, and still their gifts were vain,
Till Joshua's glory roused his fierce disdain.
Else had no proffer moved his haughty mind,
That deemed himself the champion of mankind,
When the joint wishes of the various band
To nobler Jabin gave the first command.
But Joshua's triumphs filled his anguish'd ear;
Fired at the sound, he snatched the deathful spear,
Resolved at once to prove the hero's might,
And claim, alone, the wreaths of single sight,
'Twas he, when Irad raised his dreadful voice,
And inmost Hazor trembled at the noise,
When prudent Jabin urged a nightly storm,
Ere the Youth's voice the slumbering camp should arm:
Bade his vast squadrons in the wood delay,
Nor lift a spear, till morn should lead the day.
Shall this brave host the unmanly path pursue,
Fight ambush'd foes, and basely creep from view?
Shall Jobab, like the thief, to conquest steal,
And bravery call, what coward minds can feel?
And now, from Jabin the proud chief demands,
To lead, as first in place, the central bands.
He, coolly wise, resigns the shadowy name,
And, pleased with substance, boasts a nobler fame.
Forth from the host, in steely pomp, he strode*
And 'twixt the embattled lines sublimely stood.
His towering stride, vast height, and awful arms
Chilled all his foes, and scattered wide alarms:
When thus the chief -- Ye sons of Israel know
The dauntless challenge of no common foe.
If in your host three heroes can be found,
(Be Joshua one) to tempt this dangerous ground,
Here shall they learn what strength informs the brave,
And find no God can shield them from the grave.
Stung with the insult cast upon his God,
To the great Leader Irad nimbly strode,
And thus -- Shall yonder heathen's haughty cry
Dare Israel's host, and Israel's God defy?
Let me this boaster whelm in instant shame,
Avenge my nation's cause, my Maker's name.
Exalted Youth! the smiling Chief replied,
This elder arm shall crop his towering pride.
Scarce in thy breast has manhood fixed her seat;
Blot not thy bloom, nor urge untimely fate.
Line 60) See Book 7, Line 165.
Brave as thou art, his strength must win the fight,
And Israel's glory sink in endless night.
Think not, he cried, of Irad's tender age,
Nor heed the mockery of yon heathen's rage.
This hand, though young, shall boast a conquering day;
Blind is wild rage, and pride an easy prey.
Here too shall Joshua's potent prayers be given,
And the blessed aid, that Virtue hopes from Heaven.
Should Irad perish, none the wound shall know;
Should Joshua fall, our race is whelmed in woe:
Heaven gave his chosen to thy guardian care,
To rule in peace, to save in dangerous war;
On thee alone our fates suspended lie,
With thee we flourish, and with thee we die.
Oh best of youths! provoke not hasty doom,
Nor rush impetuous to an early tomb.
I loved thy sire, the good, the just, the brave --
And shall this voice consign thee to the grave?
Swift thy name ripens into matchless praise;
My son, my chosen, still prolong thy days.
In future fields thy arm shall brighter shine;
Thine be the glory, but the danger mine.
Ah grant my wish! the impatient Youth replies,
While two full tears stand glistening in his eyes --
This arm, unhurt, shall bid the monster bleed;
Angels will guard my course, and Heaven succeed.
My spear, when night her latest darkness spread,
Had sunk him breathless in the field of dead;
But some kind spirit saved his life, till morn
Should grace the fight, and Irad's name adorn*
Aid me, oh aid me, Hezron's every friend!
Your voice, your wishes, must the Leader bend.
Won by his earnest cries, the generous Chief
Forced his consent; but could not hide his grief.
A sigh steals silent from his bleeding breast,
As his slow tongue permits the sad request.
Wrapped in bright arms, while smiles his joy revealed,
The Youth stalked fearless over the horrid field;
The ho^t, with rapture, viewed his lofty stride,
The leap alert, the port of conscious pride;
But each grave chief, by long experience wise,
With faltering accent, to his comrade cries --
I fear, I fear, lest, on the bloody sand,
The bold Youth perish, by yon monster's hand.
What bravery can, fair Irad will perform,
But can the opening floweret meet the storm?
Ah, that such sweetness, such etherial fire
Should fall, the victim of a heathen's ire!
Thy votary's course, all-gracious Heaven, survey!
Let some kind angel hover round his way!
Now near the scene bold Irad urged his course,
Where Jobab triumphed in resistless force;
When the huge warrior, swelled with angry pride,
With bended brow, and voice contemptuous, cried --
Art thou the champion of thy vaunting race?
Shall this poor victory Jobab's falchion grace?
Go, call great Joshua, long to war inured,
Whose arm has toils, whose skill has hosts endured,
With him, ten chiefs; this hand shall crush them all;
Shame stains the steel, that bids a stripling fall;
Retire, ere vengeance on thy helmet light;
Fly to yon troop, and save thy life by flight.
His haughty foe the Youth undaunted heard;
Vain, empty threats his bosom never feared;
Over the vast form he turned his smiling eyes,
And saw unmoved the livid vengeance rise.
Then, with a rosy blush of conscious worth,
Calm from his tongue his manly voice broke forth --
Do threats like these become a hero's voice?
Can courage find a vent in empty noise?
To every brave man give the well-earn'd praise,
Nor think on scoffs a bright renown to raise*
True bravery claims a noble generous fame;
But the base wretch from vaunts expects his name.
Let shame, let truth, those coward words recall;
Thou seek'st my life; I glory in thy fall.
To me thy pride to me thy threats are vain;
Heaven sees alone whose arm the prize shall gain.
And know, wheree'er may light his angry rod,
I fear no boaster that defies my GOD.
Now shield to shield, and lance to lance, they stand;
With taunts imperious shout the heathen band;
While hopeless Israel heaven with prayer assails,
And grateful incense fills the rising gales.
Stung by the just reproof, with whizzing sound
The giant plunged his javelin in the ground:
For passion, ever blind, impelled his arm,
Steered a wild course, and saved the youth from harm;
He, calm and fearless, with a pleased surprise,
Surveyed its curious form and mighty size;
Then against his foe, with sure, unerring eye
Drove the swift lance, and lodged it in his thigh.
Enraged, the warrior saw his bubbling gore,
Writhed with keen anguish, and the javelin tore.
The flesh pursued; a copious, sable stream
Poured from the wound, and stained the steely gleam;
Then high in air he shook his sunlike shield,
And waved his falchion over the astonished field.
With matchless force the vengeful weapon fell;
The wary hero nimbly shunned the steel;
And while his foe with foaming fury cried,
Often pierced his arm, and wounded often his side.
Wild, and more wild, the giant's strokes resound,
Glance from the shield, and plough the cleaving ground:
Till, gathering all his strength for one vast blow,
Dark as a storm, he rushes on his foe;
Lightly the hero springs; the monster falls,
Like sudden ruins of a turret's walls;
Full on his neck descends the gladsome blade,
And from the trunk disparts the grisly head.
Loud shouts of joy, from Israel's thousands driven,
Burst over the plain, and shook the walls of heaven:
Amazed the heathens saw their champion lost,
And a wide, sullen groan was heard from all the host.
Alert, bold Irad seized the giant's shield,
His sword, his spear, and bore them through the field;
At Joshua's feet, with self-approving smiles,
He cast the grandeur of the glittering spoils;
The hoary warriors gathered round his way,
And gazed and wondered at the curious prey;
Then blessed the chief, with transport in their eyes,
And owned the assistance of auspicious Skies;
While youths unhappy raised less ardent prayers,
And wished the deed, and wished the glory, theirs.
Led by soft impulse towered the imbattled train,
Roved sad Selima down the spacious plain.
Afar she stood, and cast an anxious eye,
And strove in vain her favorite to descry.
At once, with distant din, the shouts ascend,
And painful fears her tender bosom rend;
Slow towered the camp her lingering steps inclined;
But often the fair-one cast a look behind.
Now the long thunders of the clarion sound,
Reclam'd from hills, and plains, and groves around,
Over the dire field the rushing squadrons driven,
Extend their shady files, and blacken heaven:
High in the central front great Joshua stands,
And shoots wide terror through the astonished bands;
Mid eastern thousands Zimri towers along,
And Irad shines before the western throng.
Unfurled, the sudden banners stream afar,
And, wrapped in thunder, joins the dreadful war;
Wide roll the volumes of the dust around,
And clouds on clouds envelope all the ground.
As floods, increased by long-descending rains,
Pour a brown deluge over the wintery plains,
Loud from a thousand hills, the torrents join,
Where azure bonds the river's course confine;
The maddening ice, in boundless ruin driven,
Bursts, like the thunders of a falling heaven;
The white rocks foam; the gloomy blasts arise,
Toss the wild stream, and roar along the skies.
So closed the squadrons of the unnumber'd foes;
So stormy shouts and hollow groans arose.
Long in an even balance hung the affray,
Nor those would loose, nor these could gain, the day.
'Till Irad's rapid path, like heaven's red fire,
Shot through the ranks, and bade the foe retire;
With joy, their chief surrounding warriors view,
And troops on troops the generous course pursue.
At distance small, proud Samlah's glittering car,
Whirled by white coursers, tempts the grisly war;
Over all the plain, with piercing sound, arise
His stern injunctions, and his conquering cries.
With shouts bold Irad darts along the field,
Now bright in arms, and now in dust concealed,
From rank to rank the well-known chief pursues,
And often his flashing steel in blood imbrues.
Vain, impious wretch, he cried, thy nimble flight,
And vain the covert of surrounding might.
Once have thou fled the swift-pursuing spear,
But fled'st in vain, for vengeance finds thee here.
Learn from this hand what fate betides the knave,
Who yields, unmoved, a brother to the grave.
If now thy feet escape the righteous doom,
Let Heaven protect thee to a peaceful tomb!
In dread amaze astonished Samlah stood;
From his pale face retired the freezing blood;
His wild eye star'd; all bristling rose his hair:
Quick from his quiv^ring hand the useless spear
Dropped; his teeth rattled, and the falling reins
At random trembled on the coursers' manes;
Behind he gazed, and found no path to fly;
For aid he panted, but no aid was nigh.
Deep in his back was lodged the fatal steel;
His breathless form, before the rolling wheel,
Plunged headlong; mournful rung a pitying groan,
So fair, so mild his beauteous aspect shone:
Even Irad, touched by Adnor's kind request,
Felt soft emotions stealing through his breast.
Then swift he wheeled the lightening of his sword;
Behind him, Judah's host like torrents poured;
Shrill rose the tumult of the fields around,
Trembled through heaven and waved along the ground:
With souls undaunted, both the hosts contend;
Spears fill the air, and shouts the concave rend.
Far distant, Joshua moves his awful form,
Swells the confusion, and directs the storm.
Beyond him, Zimri, swift as rapid fire,
Darts through the fight, and bids the foe expire.
A mingled horror clouds the dreadful plain;
Here rush the fighting, and there fall the slain.
Now the mid sun had finished half his course,
When Irad raging with resistless force,
And far before him breathing wide dismay,
On Jabin's chariot drove his rapid way.
Brave youths around him thronged the crimson fight,
Eyed the blessed chief, and smiled a fierce delight;
From every sword increasing vengean^e fell,
And Death sat hovering over the sanguine steel.
Throned in proud state, the savage Monarch rode;
Like two red stars his wrathful eye balls glowed;
Hoarse from his voice a dreadful thunder came,
And his bright ^rmour flashed a sudden flame.
Two steeds, bedropp'd with gore, and pale to view,
Emblems of death, his smoking chariot drew.
Cheered by his hand, the coursers swiftly sprang;
Beat by their hoofs, the brazen bucklers rang;
Towered Irad's path the heathen* winged his way,
And, boding conquest, snuff'd the fancied prey.
Unmoved, the angelic Youth, with wearied hands
Paved his red path, and drove the circling bands --
Stay, lovely hero! stay; thy course forbear;
Enough that sword has ruled the glorious war --
Ah stay, till Israel's sons thy steps surround;
Return, return, and be with glory crowned!
Great Jabin stood, and over the bloody field
Raised the broad terrors of his flaming shield;
His grimly brow, all blackened over with dust,
Frowned like a storm, and froze the trembling host;
Near beauteous Irad streamed the sounding car,
And opening squadrons yield the dreadful war.
The foaming Chief, serene the Youth beheld,
And reared his javelin over the purple field;
Shrill sung the lance along the dusty sky,
Bored the strong shield, and pierced the Monarch's thigh*
Enraged, to earth the haughty Warrior sprang;
His red eyes flamed; his arms descending rang;
With lofty action, each his hand uprais'd;
The falchions flashed; aghast the squadrons gazed;
Two generous youths between them nimbly broke,
And bowed their lives beneath the fatal stroke.
Their lovely heads (their helmets cleft in twain)
Died the keen swords, and spouted on the plain.
More fierce the Monarch's disappointed ire
Glowed in his face, and blazed with gloomy fire.
In Irad, innocence serenely mild,
And beauty's sweetness with soft splendour smiled;
Round his fair forehead beams of bravery play,
Nor stained with rage, nor mingled with dismay.
Again in either rose the dreadful steel;
Again it lightened, and again it fell;
The Heathen's, ringing, leaped from Irad^^ shield;
The Youth's in fragments, treacherous, strewn the field.
Held by a chief, swift-leaping from the band,
A second falchion touched his reaching hand,
When -- loveliest Youth! why did thy buckler's bound
Shield but thy breast? why not thy form surround?
Where stood thy friends? was no kind hero near,
To guard thy life, and stay Selima's tear? --
From some base arm unseen, in covert flung,
Through his white side a coward javelin sung,
He fell -- a groan sad-murmur'd round the host,
Their joy, their glory, and their leader lost.
Forth from the train a youth impatient sprung,
Spread his fond arms, and round the hero clung,
With soft endearments stayed the fleeting breath,
And wished to save him from the hand of death.
But Jabin's sword, driven through his friendly side,
Stained his white armor with a spotless tide:
In kind embrace their heaving bosoms lay,
And all life's blooming beauty died away.
Through fields of air, their social spirits joined
Winged their light way, nor lost a look behind;
While two bright forms, on rosy pinions borne,
Sailed round their path, and opened the gates of morn.
Mid countless warriors Irad's limbs were spread,
Even there distinguished from the vulgar dead.
Fair as the spring, and bright as rising day,
His snowy bosom opened as he lay;
From the deep wound a little stream of blood
In silence fell, and on the javelin glowed.
Grim Jabin, frowning over his hapless head,
Deep in his bosom plunged the cruel blade;
Foes, even in death, his vengeance never forgave,
But hailed their doom, insatiate as the grave;
No worth, no bravery could his rage disarm,
Nor smiling love could melt, nor angel-beauty charm*
With dreadful sound, he raised his voice on high,
Froze the pale bands, and thundered through the sky --
Haste, warriors, haste; your conquering arms display;
Here gasps their leader, to the dogs a prey.
See the slaves fly; ere evening's dusky hour,
The beasts shall ^end them, and the hawks devour.
Receive, illustrious Oran! here receive
The poor, the sole reward, thy prince can give.
This victim first; a nation soon shall come
To pay due honors at thy sacred tomb,
Wide streams of gore in rich libations ^low,
And shades unnumber'd wait thy call below.
Here, dastards, here the worthless carcass yield,
Nor wait the vengeance of a future fie^d.
To day this raptured hand your camp shall burn,
And sires, and wives, and sons to mingled ashes turn.
Thus spoke the haughty Chief: with flashing eyes,
To fiercer fight inspired the warriors rise;
Clouds after clouds in gloomy pomp ascend,
And stormy clamours troubled either rend.
The thickening tempest Judah's host surveyed,
And wedged their volumes in the dusty shade;
Man locked with man, and helm with helm combined,
And sword with sword in glimmering order joined,
A long dread front, impervious, hides the fields,
Clothed with the grandeur of a thousand shields.
First, in the flaming van to vengeance rose
Bold Irad's train, and dared their ardent foes.
Their young, brave minds immortal same inspires;
Each glowing thought the patriot's virtue ^ires;
Serene they smiled to see the ruin nigh;
In death they triumphed, but they feared to fly.
Over the dark deep, as some tall wave impends,
Its white foam hisses, and its point ascends;
Against hoary rocks the bursting ruins roar,
Shake all the main, and echo ^ound the s^ore*
(...) car with gloomy terror flew,
(...) ranks that near him rashly drew;
Rolled in one mighty mass, the heathen force,
The swift-wing'd chariot, and the foaming horse,
Over all the lovely band resistless fly,
And countless warriors round their Irad die.
Thus, on the stream's fair bank in beauty rise
Young, towering trees, and feel indulgent skies;
In spring's mild beam their lovely boughs aspire,
Wave over the flowers, and call the plumy choir:
At once the floods descend, the torrents roar;
The trees lie withering on the wasted shore.
All firmly brave, imbrown'd with dust and blood
Against the rude tempest Judah's veterans stood;
Fixed, even to death, their nation to defend,
With stout, stiff strength, the stubborn ranks contend;
To fate undaunted many a hero springs,
The shouts redouble, and the concave rings.
Full in the front brave Uzal moveless stood,
His falchion reeking with incessant blood;
Fight, warriors, fight, or fall -- he said, nor more;
But wheeled his arm, and stepped in floods of gore;
Above his feet the purple torrents ran,
And high before him man was pil'd on man.
So thick the swords around his helmet hung,
That sword clave sword; aloud his armor rung;
Panting he stood; in floods the sweat distilled:
Nor moves the Hero, nor the squadrons yield.
From his bright car, that rattling poured along,
With shouts, and threatenings, Jabin fired the throng;
Man leaped over man: from every side they rushed;
Bold warriors fell* by other warriors crushed;
'Till, hurled by Jabin's hand, a javelin flew,
Pie^^'d Uzal's heart, and life's fair current drew,
Pleased, the great hero gave his parting breath;
My nation owned my life, and now demands my death.
Thus hung with wounds, a prey to savage steel,
In Princeton's fields the gallant Mercer fell.
When first his native realm her sons decreed,
In slavery's chains, with want and woe to bleed,
Checked, through his bosom fond remembrance ran,
The cause of freedom was the cause of man.
In that fair cause he barred his manly breast,
The friend, the hope, the champion, of the oppressed,
From height to height on glory's pinions rose,
Blessed by his friends, and praised by generous foes;
Swift flew the shaft; the eagle ceased to rise,
And mourning millions traced him down the skies.
He fell; the throng, that pressed against his shield,
Plunged in one heap, and spread along the field;
Bucklers on bucklers rang; steel clash'd on steel;
Their own swords gash'd them, wounding as they fell.
In one broad ruin lay the mingled crowd,
And cries, and hollow groans were heard aloud.
So some tall prop, that bears extended walls,
Mouldering, gives way; the mossy structure falls,
The long beams thundering echo round the skies,
Earth shakes beneath, and clouds of dust arise.
Thus sunk the warriors, some to rise no more,
Some, nimbly bounding, bathed their spears in gore.
Now haughty Jabin lifts a louder cry,
The tall hills echo, and the fields reply.
Fly, dastards, fly; death haunts your impious way;
Your proud name sinks; your squadrons swift decay:
Where now 's the chief, that led your hosts abroad?
Your far-fam'd bravery, and fictitious GOD?
Call the dread Power, that cleft the Egyptian wave,
To mourn your fate, and open your heads a grave.
Pour on, my heroes, while yon friendly light
Shines in the heaven, and joys to view the fight.
He spoke, and onward winged his dreadful form;
Hazor behind him, like an evening storm,
That rides on gloomy blasts above the hills,
And wakes the thunder of the mountain rills,
Rolled blackening. Israel's sons in sad dismay,
Bent towered the camp their slow, unwilling way.
Enraged Shelumiel raised his angry voice,
But raised in vain; no hero heeds the noise:
Hoarse with shrill cries, and wild with deep despair,
He rushed resistless on the thickest war,
From Jabin's lance a grateful exit found,
Sunk in his arms, and stiffen'd on the ground.
Far from the fight, despoiled of helm and shield,
Slept beauteous Irad on the mournful field;
Deaf to the groans, and careless of the cries;
His hair soft-whistling over his half-shut eyes.
On either side his lifeless arms were spread,
And blood ran round him from the countless dead.
Even there, two warriors, rushing over the plain,
Over crimson torrents, and over piles of sl^in,
Stopped, when the lovely form arose to sight,
Surveyed his charms, and wished no more the fight.
Ah! hapless Youth! cried one, with tender voice,
The Gods' fair offspring, formed for milder joys!
A face like thine the gentlest thoughts must move,
The gaze of Beauty, and the song of Love.
Sleep on, fair hero! for thy corse must lie
Bare to the fury of a stormy sky.
Thus he. His friend, by softer passions warmed,
By grief afflicted, and by beauty charmed,
Cries sadly -- No; for when my steps return,
This bleeding breast thy early fate shall mourn;
The melting song declare thy hapless doom,
And my own hand erect thy head a tomb.
But now, outspread over all the northern plain,
In sable grandeur rolled a countless train,
With trembling spears, with waving bucklers, bright,
And the quick gleams of interrupted light.
When Joshua strode the heathen host to dare,
To guard the camp was prudent Caleb's care.
He, coolly wise, had summoned all the train,
Disposed in ranks, and guided over the plain,
All armed for war, at distance meet to stay,
And wait the changes of the dreadful day.
In even scale while dubious combat hung,
And far in southern fields the tumult rung,
Silent, they listened to the blended cry,
And heard faint shouts in distant murmurs die.
But now the approaching clarion's dreadful sound
Denounces flight, and shakes the banner'd ground;
From clouded plains increasing thunders rise,
And drifted volumes roll along the skies.
At once the chief commands; the unnumber'd throng,
Like gathering tempests, darkly poured along:
High on the winds, unfurled in purple pride,
The imperial standard cast the view aside;
A hero there sublimely seemed to stand,
To point the conquest, and the flight command;
In arms of burnished gold the warrior shone,
And waved and brightened in the falling sun.
Swift towered the fight approached the impatient throng,
And wider poured the thickening dust along;
Loud, and more loud, victorious clamours grow,
And, more distinguished, breathe the sounds of woe;
Pale Judah's sons a yielding fight maintain,
And many a face looks backward over the plain,
When Caleb's mighty voice, in thunder driven,
Starts all the host, and rends the clouded heaven.
What dismal scenes, enraged the hero cries --
Convulse this heart, and pierce these bleeding eyes!
Shall Judah's race, my brethren and my boast,
Flee, vanquished, driven, before a heathen host?
Can men, can warriors own so black a part,
The best of chiefs, your Joshua to desert?
Say with what pangs will Heaven the wretches try,
That know no honor, and that feel no tie?
On yon bright plain, the conquering Chief behold,
Troops winged before him, cars tumultuous rolled,
With Heaven's imperial sword the fight commands,
And drives fierce ruin over decreasing bands!
Say, shall the Man, who fights, who bleeds for all,
See your base flight, and perish in your fall?
The Chief, as angels kind, as angels true,
Sink in the doom, he warded long from you?
Fly then; but know, a few short furlongs past,
Yon camp wild flames, and savage swords shall waste;
Besmeared with streaming blood, your parents lie,
And, dashed on stones, your gasping infants die;
Your wives, betrayed by such base culprits, feel
Abuse, more dreadful than the griding steel?
No arm, no sword the falling nation save,
But this dire evening open our common grave.
^an these dread scenes even dastards fail to arm?
Spring from the trance, and burst the sleepy charm;
Rise, rise like men; with shame, with vengeance burn;
Wipe foul disgrace, and swift to fight return.
And ye brave chiefs, that never knew to yield,
Or turn a backward foot from glory's field,
But, led by me, the van's bright honors claim,
Smile at fair death, and shrink from torturing shame;
Lift high the avenging sword, from pity free,
And cleave the wretch that basely dares to flee.
He spoke: the sound their manly bosoms sir'd,
Wheeled their long ranks, and every arm inspired;
Even cowards now to generous combat armed,
And fainting heroes with new vengeance warmed:
Fierce Hazor's sons with equal fury driven,
Like one wide cloud, that shades the skirts of even,
Rushed dark and dreadful: ranks, by ranks impelled,
Felt the keen lance, and heaped the streaming field.
Poised in a dire suspense, the combat hung;
Swords clash'd, mail rattled, striking bucklers rung;
Here his bold ranks great Caleb's arm inspired:
There Jabin's mighty hand his warriors fired:
No more the foaming steeds could trace their way,
So thick the squadrons wedged their black array:
Loud tumults roar, the clouded heavens resound,
And deep convulsions heave the laboring ground.
Meantime, great Joshua, lightening over the plain,
Hedged his dire path with heaps of ghastly slain;
Back rolled the squadrons; death's encircling shade
Involved his course, and hovered over his head.
At once a quivering voice fair Irad named,
Announc'd his ruin, and the flight proclaimed;
From ranks to trembling ranks, the mournful sound
Waked a sad groan, and breathed a gloom around,
With livid paleness clouded every face,
Congealed each vein, and stopped the growing chase.
On the far camp they turned a frequent view;
Their fainting falchions scarce the fig (...) renew:
Thronged in a blackening storm, the foe descends;
Swift drive the chariots; far the dust extends.
With smiles, bold heathens hail commencing flight;
Their lances shower; their eye balls flash delight.
Loud as old ocean beats the rocky shore,
Loud as the storm's deep-bursting thunders roar,
Vast shouts unrolling rend the etherial round,
Trembles all heaven, and shakes the gory ground.
Amazed, the Hero saw the wild despair:
Nor knew the cause, 'till Irad filled the air;
Irad, re-echoing with a fearful noise,
Pal'd the blank face, and froze the faltering voice.
Loud over the bellowing shouts resounds his cry --
My sons, my heroes, whither will ye fly?
Will ye pursue the camp? desert the slain?
And leave your Irad on the bloody plain?
Alas! you fly to more tremendous fates;
There ruin seeks you, and base death awaits:
There, in sad horror, will your eyes behold
Flames round your camp, your wives, your children rolled:
Let vengeance rouse, let Israel's name inspi^e,
Let danger steel you, and let Irad fire,
Turn, turn, this instant seals your final doom;
You gain the day, or fall without a tomb.
He said, and waved his broad, ensanguin'd shield;
Turn, warriors, turn, resounds along the field;
A newborn bravery fires the meanest soul:
Thick spears protend; ranks lengthening onward roll:
Less loud fierce whirlwinds through the valley pour:
Less loud broad flames the spiry town devour,
When, winged by blasts, red conflagrations rise,
Blaze in the cloud-capp'd towers, and scorch the skies.
Black drifts of dust smoke through the vast profound*
Shouts hoarsely rage, and hollow groans resound.
As, when through ether's fields dark storms are driven,
The swift-wing'd flame, descending, kindles heaven,
Scath'd by the dreadful stream, the huge pines fall,
And bursting glory wraps the smoking ball;
Over the tall mountains rolls the voice of GOD,
The plains all tremble, and the forests nod:
So swift, so bright, the rushing hero poured;
With every stroke his sword a life devoured;
Full on his foes he bore resistless storm,
Pale squadrons opening to his angry form;
His shield blazed horror, and his lofty hand
Fell, with swift ruin, on the lessening band;
Gash'd by his hand, the coursers burst their reins,
And hurled their riders on the bloody plains;
Gash'd by his hand, the prostrate riders die;
Crack the round wheels, the splendid trappings sly.
Meantime, far eastward Asher crowds the war,
Nor heeds the terrors of the rattling car.
Swift as on wings of fire a meteor driven,
Mounts over the hills, and sweeps the nightly heaven,
When the pale wanderer, lost in devious ways,
With bristling hair, starts at the sudden blaze,
Rushed rapid Zimri through the parting host;
Marked by his eye the hapless foe was lost;
Over quivering ranks his sword incessant hung;
Loud in their ears his voice funereal rung
Death's hideous peal; hard-following on the sound
Sunk the last stroke, and corses clothed the ground.
Now while the Hittites sled the dire alarm,
Their haughty king withstood the invading arm.
Shrill rose the thunders of his piercing cry,
Lost in deaf ears, and echoing through the sky;
With swifter steps, his warriors urged their flight,
And dark behind them rushed pursuing night.
Fierce on the king's bright car, with rapid force,
Resistless Zimri drove his dreadful course;
The dauntless monarch cast his mighty spear,
That sung, and trembled through the enlightened air;
Full on brave Zimri's helm the polished steel
Clash'd harmless, and to earth, rebounding, sell.
Regardless of the shock, the nimble chief
Sprang to the car; no sword could lend relief;
Caught by his arm, the heathen beat the ground;
Wide on his bosom sunk the fatal wound;
The greedy blade, deep-plunging, gash'd his side,
And down his buckler poured a bubbling tide.
Winged with fierce ardour, Zimri mounts the car,
And calls his heroes to the crimson war. --
Rush on to conquest, every generous band,
Lo the blessed triumphs of this happy hand!
Here, through his side the sword indignant thrust,
Their furious leader, gasping, bites the dust. --
Fly, miscreants, fly, and let your lives remain
To grace the falchions of a future plain.
From (...) like foes what warrior hopes a name?
(...) the purchase, victory scarce is fame. --
(...), loud and taunting, rose the hero's cry;
Swift rush his bands; the heathen swifter fly:
High in the chariot, in dread pomp revealed,
His gloomy hand the firey steeds impelled;
In dusty clouds the hosts are snatched from sight,
And Death, and Zimri, darken over the flight.
While thus brave Asher trod the conquering plain,
And drove wild ruin on the heathen train,
In the dire center, to resistless war
Proud Shimron's monarch urged the thundering car.
In early youth, he saw fierce Jabin's hand
Seize his fair crown, and rule his fertile land;
Then to the victor's court a captive brought,
In arms was trained, in arts politic taught,
Won by soft wiles, his throne of Jabin held,
And bade his realm imperial tributes yield.
There, fired to glory by the monarch's voice,
He mocked his pattern, and obeyed his choice,
And hoped from conduct, formed by rules so just,
Alone to reign, when Jabin slept in dust.
Full on his lofty breast the flashing shield
Gleam'd a bright terror through the clouded field:
As when the Sun, over scorched Peruvia's plain,
Disease, and Death, and Horror in his train,
Unveils his crimson face, distained with blood,
Burns the brown hills, and sickens every flood.
Loud rang the hero's voice; his lances flew,
And every lance the foremost warrior slew.
On him great Joshua glanced a darkening eye,
And rushed impetuous, with a deathful cry:
His sword, swift-circling, hewed his dismal way,
Felled ranks at once, and broke the deep array.
Amazed, the heathen cast a look behind,
And thus in doubt, explored his mighty mind* --
Shall I resisting dare that arm of death,
And ^each his heart, or nobly yield my breath*
Or with some distant band the foe engage
Where bravery fail^, and turn the battle's rage?
This arm, this spear may spill his hated life;
And O what wreaths shall crown the happy strife!
What bright rewards shall Jabin's hand bestow!
What matchless honors round my temples flow!
I claim the contest -- hence base flight and shame --
To fight is glory, and to die is fame.
He spoke; while Ruin, riding through the plain,
Burst over his ranks, and marked her path with slain:
On Joshua's helm she sat; tremendous hung
His arm on high, his voice like thunder rung:
Near the bright car he wheeled his streaming blade,
And dust around him cast a night-like shade.
Full on his buckler clash'd the heathen's spear,
Pierced the thick plates, and flashed behind in air;
Grazing his side, it cut the folded garb,
And drops of crimson stained the polished barb.
With joy, the king his faithful javelin viewed,
Leaped from his car, and with his sword pursued.
Then Joshua's hand uprear'd his falchion high,
Its flames bright-circling in the dusky sky;
First his foe's arm dropped on the bloody field;
The second stroke divides his glittering shield;
Full on his throat the fierce avenging blade
Sinks; the freed spirit flits to midnight shade.
"Pour on to glory" -- rung the Leader's voice,
The trembling host shrunk backward at the noise;
Sad Shimron's sons beheld their monarch dead,
Raised one deep howl, and, winged with horror, fled.
Thronged in a gloomy storm, their headlong foes
Round the dire slight with listed falchions rose;
Broad streams of blood o'er-ran the scenes of death,
And sullen groans proclaimed the parting breath*
As boiling Etna rolls a flood of fire
Down her rough rocks; and plains, and towns expire,
Licked by the flames, exhaling rivers rise,
And crumbling groves smoke upward to the skies,
Swift pours the blazing deluge on the shore,
The scorched main foams, the hissing billows roar:
So fierce and dreadful, flew the victor host,
In night involved, in dusty volumes lost.
Squadrons thick-strown were scattered over the fields.
And helms, and swords, and spears, and sanguine shields.
Huge piles of slaughter gathering round his course,
On Shimron Joshua winged his mighty force.
Like two red flames his vivid eye balls glow,
And shoot fierce lightenings on the astonished foe;
Before, expanded, his meteorous shield
Blazed a broad ruin through the stormy field;
Round the wild war his flashing terrors fly;
Cars burst before him; -- steeds, and heroes die.
So rushed an angel down the midnight gloom,
When Egypt's firstborn sunk in one broad tomb;
High in dark clouds the avenging Vision hung,
His path, like distant thunder, hoarsely rung*
Flames shot before him, whirlwinds rolled around,
Bowed the tall hills, and heaved the trembling ground.
Not with less terror blazed the Leader on;
'Twas ruin all and one unbounded groan;
None looked behind, none turned a hearkening ear;
Nor hills, nor streams impede the full career:
High over the ragged rocks they nimbly bound,
Dash through the floods, and scower the level ground:
First in the tumult, Youth impels his flight;
Springs over the field, and scapes pursuing night:
Pale Age with quivering limb^, and slow-drawn pace,
Feels the keen sword, and sinks beneath the chase.
Far distant, Zimri, like a sweeping storm.
Crim in the chariot raised his gloomy form;
Still on the hindmost fell his fateful sword;
Earth shook, air trembled, heaven with thunder roared:
Often, from the car descending to the plain,
He streamed, like lightening, over the ghastly slain,
Then swiftly rose, and on the heathens sped,
His wheels dark-rolling over the unnumber'd dead.
Meantime, with all the rage of combat fired,
While throngs of warriors round his steps expired;
While now, first disobedient to his call,
The balanced victory doubted where to fall:
While Caleb's arm with youthful vigor warmed,
Shamed Judah's thousands and their vengeance armed;
From rank to rank impatient Jabin flew,
Drove these with threats, and those with praises drew.
But now the eastern plain loud thunders rend;
The shrill cars rattle; hoarser cries ascend;
Progressive clouds, in thickening volumes driven,
Roll towered the south, and shade the dusty heaven.
From the tall car the Chief surveyed the field,
And every circling scene at once beheld,
Even the far wood, with sudden flashes bright,
And the dire omens of tumultuous flight.
Around the war he cast a searching view,
Saw the day lost, and all its evils knew;
Deep from his inmost soul burst forth a sigh,
And momentary sadness gloom'd his eye.
But soon his brow resumed a cheerful grace,
And living ardour fired his artful face.
Full well the monarch knew that fears begun,
From breast to breast, like glancing lightenings, run;
That one rank fled instructs a host to fly,
And cowards' eyes teach heroes' hearts to die --
Then, ere his friends the dire event divine,
Or Judah's sons their kindred victors join,
A wise retreat his mighty mind ordained,
And thus the rage of war his voice restrained.
Hear, all ye chiefs, brave Hazor's bands that guide,
Your nation's pillars, and your monarch's pride.
Your matchless deeds this raptured eye has told,
And fame's bright hand to distant years enrolled.
But see, over western hills the sun's low fire
Cuts short the day, and bids the host retire.
Firm be your ranks, man fast inlock'd with man,
The rear led onward, fixed the generous van;
At once let chief with chief inspired combine,
And against the foe extend the embattled line;
Brace firm the shield; the moveless spear protend;
Join hand and heart, and every rank defend.
Your prince behold; when Hazor claims the strife,
My wounds are transport, and a toy my life.
The hero spoke: as by one soul inspired,
Swift to their well-known posts the chiefs retired;
At once, by banners rang'^ (...) brave the storm,
Firm, dreadful lines the (...) squadrons form.
Dire over the vanguard, sh^^^d with shield combined,
Spear locked with spear, the undaunted leaders joined;
Against Judah's host, with ridgy terrors bright,
Rose a long wall, and flashed a fearful light.
Over the tremendous scene the Monarch's car
Poured death around, and ruled the grisly war:
Fierce on the foe, wherever their steps pursue,
From rank to rank the mighty warrior flew;
Hearts formed of stubborn steel his deeds appall;
The distant tremble, and the nearer fall;
Till Caleb's voice commands the chase to stay,
And yields his foes an unmolested way.
Then, still and slow, while Judah's host admired,
In gloomy strength the sullen storm retired.
So, when in heaven propitious breezes rise,
And on the deep the nimble vessel flies,
Shagg'd with brown shades, that over the billows lower,
In grim, dark pomp recedes the clifted shore;
Less seen, and less, the awful scenes decay,
And lost in blue confusion fade away.
With gore all hideous, and with dust imbrown'd,
In the dire front terrific Jabin frowned;
His lifted arm prepared the fatal blow,
And menaced vengeance to the approaching foe. --
So, forward driven by earth's convulsive pangs,
The tall, hoar cliff in dubious terror hangs;
High poised in dread suspense, its hovering brow
Lowers swift destruction on the world below:
Amazed, the swain, while sudden fears appall
Starts, as the tottering ruin seems to fall.
Enjoy, he cried, imperious foes, enjoy
The fancied triumph, combat shall destroy:
But know, ye boasters, soon this arm shall tear
The short-lived crown, your haughty temples wear;
Soon your vain chiefs, your nation want a name,
And all your glories sink in endless shame.
But now, sublime in crimson triumph borne,
The sacred standard mocked the etherial morn;
Wide on the winds its waving splendors flowed,
And called the warriors from the distant wood.
Behind great Joshua, Hazor's sons to dare,
Pour the bold thousands to the western war,
Beyond Ai's walls, the lessening heathen train
In well-form'd squadrons cross the distant plain:
Part still in sight their shady files extend;
Part fill the wood, and part the hills ascend;
To cease from toil the prudent Chief commands,
And balmy quiet sooths the wearied bands.
Half lost in mountain groves, the sun's broad ray
Shower'd a full splendour round his evening way;
Slow Joshua strode the lovely Youth to find*
The unwilling bands more slowly moved behind.
Soon as the matchless form arose to view,
Over their sad faces shone the sorrowing dew;
Silent they stood. To speak the Leader tried,
But the choked accents on his palate died.
His bleeding bosom beat with inward pains,
And leaden languors ran along his veins.
Ah, best and bravest of thy race! he said,
And gently raised the pale, re^lining head --
Lost are thy matchless charms, thy glory gone --
Gone is the glory which thy hand has won.
In vain on thee thy nation cast her eyes;
In vain with joy beheld thy light arise;
In vain she wished thy scepter to obey;
Vain were her wishes; vain the destined sway.
Oh! Irad, loveliest Irad, nature's pride!
Would Heaven, myself for thee, for thee had died!
Nor more; the thoughts lay struggling in his breast;
But tears, expressive tears forbade the rest.
Borne by six chiefs, in silence, over the plain,
Fair Irad moved before the mournful train;
Great Joshua's arm sustained his sword, and shield;
The afflicted thousands lengthening through the field.
When, crowned with flowers, the maidens at her side.
With gentle steps advanced great Caleb's pride.
Her snowy hand, inspired by restless love,
Of the lone wild-rose two rich wreaths inwove;
Fresh in her hand the flowers rejoice to bloom,
And round the fair-one shed the mild perfume.
Over all the train her active glances roved;
She gazed, and gazing, missed the Youth she loved;
Some dire mischance her boding heart divined,
And thronging terrors filled her anxious mind.
As near the host her quickening footsteps drew,
The breathless hero met her trembling view;
From her chilled hand the headlong roses fell,
And life's gay beauty bade her cheeks farewell;
Over her fair face unmeaning paleness sat,
And, sunk to earth, she felt no hapless fate.
With anguish Caleb saw her fading charms,
And caught the favorite in his hastening arms.
Revived with piercing voice, that froze his soul,
She forced the big, round tear unwish'd to roll;
By all his love, besought him soon to lead
Where cruel friendship snatched his lovely dead.
In vain the chief his anguish strove to hide,
Sighs rent his breast, and chilled the vital tide.
To Joshua then, whose heart beside her mourned,
With gaze of keen distress, the charmer turned. --
Oh, generous Chief, to misery ever kind, --
Thou love my fire -- support his sinking mind!
Thy friendly wish delights to lessen woe --
See how his tears for fallen Irad flow!
He claims thy friendship -- generous hero, see,
Lost to himself, his fondness bleeds for me. --
To view th^^ hapless Youth, distressed he fears.
Would wound my soul, and force too copious tears.
But lead, oh lead me, where the Youth is borne!
Calm is my heart, nor will my bosom mourn --
So cold that heart, it yields no pitying sigh --
And see no tear bedews this marbled eye.
She said, and looked resistless; soft reclined
On Joshua's arm, she forced his melting mind.
Pressing her hand, he traced a gentle way,
Where breathless Irad, lost in slumbers lay.
From the pale face his chilling hand withdrew
The decent veil, and gave the Youth to view.
Fixed over the form, with solemn gaze she hung,
And strong, deep sighs burst over her frozen tongue.
On Joshua then she cast a wishful look;
Wild was her tearless eye, and rolling spoke
Anguish unutterable. Thrice she tried
To vent her woes, and thrice her effort, died.
At length, in accents of ecstatic grief,
Her voice bewildered, gave her heart relief.
Is this the doom we dread? -- is this to die?
To sleep? -- to feel no more? -- to close the eye? --
Slight is the change -- how vain the childish fear*
That trembles, and recoils, when death is near?
I too, methinks, would share the peaceful doom,
And seek a calm repose in Irad's tomb.
This breath I know, this useless breath must fail,
These eyes be darkened, and this face grow pale --
But thou art pale, oh Youth! thy lot I crave,
And every grief shall vanish in the grave.
She ceased, the tender chief without delay,
Soft pressing, kindly forced her steps away.
Slow towered the camp, with solemn pace, they drew;
The corse moves on; the mournful bands pursue.
Pale Uzal follows, virtuous now no more;
And brave Shelumiel, black with clotted gore.
Unnumber'd tears their hapless fate bewail,
And voice to voice resounds the dreadful tale.
But Irad, matchless Irad, called in vain,
Breathes wide a solemn sadness round the plain:
Unhappy, to their tents the host retired,
And gradual; over the mountains day expired*
THE CONQUEST OF CANAAN. BOOK IX.

ARGUMENT.
Evening. Interview between Selima and her parents. Morning. Distress of the
Camp. Joshua directs Zimri to bury the dead. Funeral of Irad. Burial of the
dead. Hareshah informs Joshua of a combination of the surrounding nations
against Gibeon, and solicits his assistance. Story of Elam and Mina. Hareshah
is directed to wait until the divine pleasure shall be known. Eveneng. Joshua
walks out on the plain, northward of the camp, and hears Selima lamenting the
death of Irad. Affected by the scene, he breaks out into a soliloquy on hi^
distress, and is reproved by an angel, who delivers him a message from the Most
High, and directs him to prepare for a vision of futurity.

THE CONQUEST OF CANAAN. BOOK IX.
NOW sober evening hung her curtains round,
And gloomy sadness brooded over the ground.
All pale, and solemn, rose the languid moon,
And shed a feeble twilight from her throne.
Sad in her tent, the feeling maiden sat,
Fed on her woes, and sighed her hapless fate.
Dissolved in tears, her render parents came,
To share her grief, and stay life's parting flame.
Like dull, cold lights, that hover over the tomb,
A lone lamp languish'd round the silent room:
Beside her couch, two lorn attendants stayed,
And drooping, lingering, eyed the unconscious maid.
Over the sad scene the pair attentive hung;
Then round the favorite form all-anxious clung:
Her tearless eye balls scarce the virgin turned,
But, fixed in blank despair, her slumbering Irad mourned.
Awake! oh wake! the tender mother cried --
My child! my darling! nature's loveliest pride!
Awake, and hear! oh hear thy mother's call!
Behold these tears for thee in anguish fall!
Ah see thy sire, with mighty woes oppressed!
His sighs hard-bursting from his heaving breast!
Turn, turn thine eye! thy hapless parents save!
Nor speed our footsteps to the dreary grave!
She spoke. Overwhelmed in bitterness of fate,
Still the sweet maiden unregardful sat:
Fixed on the parent, drooped her failing eyes*
And deep, and heavy, heaved her long-drawn sighs.
Again the mother, lost in sad amaze,
Cast on her woes a strong, expressive gaze*
And thus -- O child of parents once too blessed!
Let not such anguish tear thy bleeding breast.
Swell not, with other pangs, thy miseries dire,
A dying mother, and a widowed sire:
The balm of patience summon to thy soul:
Let Heaven's high voice excessive grief control.
He called, from earth's dark wild, the Youth away;
And called complacent, to the world of day.
To nobler scenes his mind seraphic flies,
To bliss, to Hezron, angels, and the skies.
Thus spoke the parent. Struggling rose the fair,
And looked unmeasured woe, and blank despair:
Again she languish'd; to the couch she fell,
And life sad-lingering seemed to bid farewell.
Pierced to the soul, the tender father stood,
And, lost in woes like here is, the darling viewed,
