And all yon changeless stars, that, throned on high,
Reign in immortal luster round the sky,
In solemn silence shroud their living light.
And leave the world to undistinguished night.
Hark, what dread sounds, descending from the pole,
Wave following wave, in swelling thunders roll!
How the tombs cleave! What awful forms arise!
What crowding nations pain the failing eyes!
From land to land behold the mountains rend;
From shore to shore the final flames ascend,
Round the dark poles with boundless terror reign,
With bend immeasurable sweep the main,
From morn's far kingdoms stretch to realms of even,
And climb, and climb, with solemn roar to heaven.
What smoky ruins wrap the lessening ground!
What firey sheets sail through the vaulted round!
Line 759) Resurrection and Conflagration. 787] Last Judgment.
Poured in one mass, the lands, and seas, decay;
Enrolled, the heavens, dissolving, fleet away;
The moon departs; the sun's last beams expire,
And nature's buried in the boundless fire.
Lo, from the radiance of the blessed abode,
Messiah comes, in all the pomp of GOD!
Borne on swift winds, a storm before him flies;
Stars crown his head, and rainbows round him rise;
Beneath his feet, a sun's broad terrors burn,
And cleaving darkness opes a dreadful morn:
Through boundless space careering flames are driven;
Truth's sacred hosts descend, and all the thrones of heaven.
See crowding millions, called from earth's far ends,
See hell's dark world, with fearful gloom, ascends,
In throngs incomprehensible! Around
Worlds after worlds, from nature's farthest bound,
Called by the Archangel's voice, from either pole,
Self-mov'd, with all created nations, roll.
From this great train, his eyes the just divide,
Price of his life, and being's fairest pride;
Robbed by his mighty hand, the starry throngs
From harps of transport call exstatic songs.
Hail, heirs of endless peace! ordained to rove
Round the pure climes of everlasting love.
For yon the sun first led the lucid morn;
The world was fashioned, and Messiah born;
For yon high heaven with fond impatience waits,
Pours her fair streams, and opes her golden gates;
Each hour, with purer glory, gayly shines,
Her courts enlarges, and her air refines.
But O unhappy race! to woes consigned,
Lured by fond pleasure, and to wisdom blind.
What new Messiah shall the spirit save,
Stay the pent flames, and shut the eternal grave?
Where sleeps the music of his voice divine?
Where hides the face, that could so sweetly shine?
Now hear that slighted voice to thunder turn!
See that mild face with flames of vengeance burn!
High over your heads the storm of ruin roars,
And, round the immense no friend your fate deplores.
Lo, there to endless woe in throngs are driven,
What once were angels, and bright stars of heaven!
The world's gay pride! the king with splendour crowned!
The chief resistless, and the sage renowned!
Down, down, the milli^^s sink; where yon broad main
Heaves her dark wave^, and spreads the seats of pain:
Where long, black clouds, emblaz'd with awful fire,
Pour sullen round their heads, and in dread gloom retire.
Then, tumult's hideous din forever over,
All foes subdued, and doomed to rise no more,
Sin forced from each fair clime to final flight,
And hell's dark prison locked in endless night;
To heaven's extremes diviner peace shall roll,
And spread through countless worlds, beyond each distant pole.
Crowned with glad triumph, from the toils of war,
On angel's wings, shall sail Messiah's car;
To the great Sire his conquering hand restore
The etherial ensigns of unmeasured power;
Present his sons, before the palace bright,
And seek the bosom of unborrow'd light.
Then scenes, in heaven before unknown, shall rise,
And a new era bless the angelic skies;
Through boundless tracts, a nobler kingdom shine,
Nor Seraphs' minds conceive the pomp divine.
All realms, all worlds above, combined in one;
The heaven of heavens the bright, eternal throne;
The subjects saints; the period endless spring;
The realm immensity, and GOD the king.
As fixed, unchanged, yon central world of fire
Leads on sublime the planetary choir,
Line 831) Consummation of all things.
Lights all the living lamps, and round the sky,
In midnight splendour calls the moon to fly;
Creates their smiles, instructs their orbs to roll,
Fair eye of nature, and the world's great soul:
So, in the beams of clear perfections shrin'd,
Shall his great Source, the Uncreated Mind,
Through all the Morning Stars that round him glow,
Rove in his smiles, and at his altar bow,
Through countless trains, where worlds unnumber'd rise,
And clothed in starry pomp superior skies,
Pure rays of endless peace indulgent shine,
And warm immensity with love divine.
Love's mighty chain shall boundless beings bind,
Join world to world, and mind unite with mind;
Over the great household heaven's eternal pride,
From age to age, the Almighty Sire preside;
Around his awful throne, with searching eyes,
See fairer sons, and priests, and kings, arise;
Bid his own essence in their hearts revive,
His beauty brighten, and his glory live:
From harps etherial living raptures fall,
Heaven fill the immense, and GOD BE ALL IN ALL.
In glory wafted down the lucid pole,
See Salem's walls their solemn scenes unroll!
Less beauteous charms the lovely spouse array,
When beams of rapture light the bridal day.
Behold, new skies serenely round her glow;
Pure fragrance breathes, and purple splendors flow:
In pomp ascends the ever-rising morn,
And starry rainbows round her chariot burn!
There, from the distant wave, no suns arise;
No moon's pale radiance gleams in evening skies;
Round the broad region, with unfading ray,
JEHOVAH smiles immeasurable day:
Line 875) Prospect of heaven, and a happy immortality.
With living luster, fruits celestial glow,
And streams of life in endless beauty flow.
In robes of angels, see the chosen shine;
Waft on the floods, or walk in light divine;
Or taste the changing tree, whose fruit supplies
The youth of heaven, and beauty of the skies!
There, dressed in bloom, and young in rosy years,
The immortal Father of mankind appears:
In clear effulgence, Israel's Prophet shines,
And no dark veil his eager wish confines:
With smiles of joy serene, the Friend of GOD
Counts his glad sons, and opes the blessed abode.
To these fair realms thy footsteps shall ascend:
Here crowns await thee, and bright robes attend;
At nature's call, thy guardian seraph come,
And guide his chosen to the eternal home;
Before the sacred throne, thy thoughts appear,
Thy virtuous toils, thy truth, and love, sincere:
His witnessed favorite, GOD with smiles approve,
And join to nations of immortal love.
O blissful hour! when, freed from bonds of clay,
Thy path commences to the climes of day;
When from the sun thy wing begins to rise
Through the broad regions of unmeasured skies,
When time's dark years behind thy flight shall roll,
And all eternity invade thy soul.
In that blessed hour, the sons of light shall come,
And shout thee welcome to thy destined home;
With heightening beauty bloom each angel mind,
Glow with pure joy, and yearn with love refined;
In strains divine, impassioned seraphs tell
How with dire treason heavenly nations fell;
What deeds renowned have graced the fair abode;
Truth that endured, and zeal that raised to GOD;
How round the expansion worlds unnumber'd sprung,
And hosts etherial sky-born praises sung;
The peace, the charms, to vernal Eden given,
Conversing angels, and approving Heaven.
In that blessed hour, shall saints of ancient days,
Lights of mankind, and heirs of deathless praise,
Disclose how Adam's sons the world overspread,
Borne to far isles, and over wide seas conveyed;
How the lone ark the seeds of nations bore,
And boundless ocean tossed without a shore;
Embattled hosts the patriarch's faith o'ercame,
Nor votive Isaac quenched the living flame;
Through the long devious desert Israel roved;
The angel wrestled, and the brother loved.
Rapt in thy blessed arrival, there shall glow
The faithful partners of thine every woe;
Their hopes, their fears, their toils, with thee run over,
Pains far retired, and griefs that haunt no more;
His long-lov'd friend unspotted Hezron join,
Add song to song, and mingle bliss with thine;
Irad, divinest flower! to meet thee rise,
And cast rich fragrance round delighted skies.
With this great concourse lost in joys serene,
No tongue can utter, and no fancy feign,
Dissolved in friendship, chained to friends, divine,
Whose thoughts, whose converse, every power refine,
Thy unknown ages swift shall glide away,
Lost in the immense of never-ending day.
Through heaven's expanded field thy feet shall rove,
The all-beauteous region of ecstatic love;
Her gates of pearl, her towers of gems, behold,
Her streets, her mansions, of pellucid gold.
Where each fair gate cherubic watchmen guard,
And GOD, approving, showers the vast reward.
There shall thou feel, when, freed from sin's alloy,
Souls lift their pinions to the climes of joy,
Around all heaven what speechless transports roll,
Blend smile with smile, and mingle soul with soul;
There hail, ecstatic, to the bright abode.
The crowns, the trophies, of Messiah's blood.
There GOD'S own hand shall lift the curtain high,
And all earth's wonders open to thine eye:
In time's mysterious reign, thy soul purs^e
Power ever glorious, wisdom ever new;
See boundless good, Creation's single end,
And GOD his own, and being's, faithful friend;
In all, the present GOD refulgent shine,
And boundless glory fill the work divine.
Fed with perennial springs of bliss refined,
Divine effusions of the All-lovely Mind,
With endless ardour shall thy spirit glow,
And love immense from heaven's great fountain flow;
Unbounded grace fill unconfined desire,
Warm thy rapt bosom, and thy songs inspire.
Each hour, thy spreading thoughts shall swift improve;
Each hour increase the transports of thy love;
With morning beauty, Youth around thee shine,
Implant new senses, and the old refine;
From height to height thy rising wishes grow,
And, at their birth, the full enjoyment flow;
No care, no want, the expanding bliss destroy,
But every thought, and sense, and wish, be joy.
From these blessed scenes thy flight shall often descend,
And, with thy kindred angels, man attend.
What sweet complacence shall thy bosom warm,
To spread fair truth, and every woe to charm;
Guard the lone cot, where faith delights to dwell;
Or wake pure fervors in the secret cell;
Or watch that house, where strong devotions rise;
And prayers as incense cheer the morning skies;
Where sons to saints, to angels daughters, grow,
And peace, and virtue, build a heaven below.
When fear alarms, shall thou that fear allay;
When grief distresses, smile the pangs away;
When pain torments, the pious eyelids close,
Make soft the bed, and breathe serene repose;
Guide the departing soul to yonder skies,
And teach the young immortal how to rise.
Through sco^ching sands shall thou the wanderer bring,
Waft balmy gales, and point the cooling spring;
Or lure declining feet from flowery ways,
Seal the charmed ear, and turn the fatal gaze;
Or with rude whirlwinds the rough main deform;
Or roll the thunders of the mountain storm;
Or on the sanguine plain sublimely stand,
Direct the triumph, and the ^light command;
Or over some realm in glorious pomp preside,
To saints a guardian, and to kings a guide.
Nor shall one world thy bounded view confine;
But round all being stretch thy flight divine,
To worlds dispersed over worlds, ambitious rise,
The golden planets of sublimer skies.
Far over thy little earth, to man's weak eye,
Encircling roll the glories of the sky.
Yet know, blessed prince though thus apparent all,
The moon moves singly round this darksome ball,
The earth, with those fair fires of wandering light,
That shed soft luster over the darksome night,
All worlds alike, with countless nations crowned,
In circling course, the sun's bright orb surround.
Still their glad faces to his splendour turn.
Imbibe his beams, and meet the grateful morn.
This mighty scene thy mind with awe inspires,
With beauty raptures, and with wonder fires.
But O thou man beloved! yon vault survey,
Where stars in millions blind the midnight ray;
In space' broad fields so far the pomp retires,
Yon sapphire concave scarce their twinkling fires:
Hence vainly deemed the gems of inborn light,
Ordained to tremble through the gloom of night:
In near approach, those stars, with constant rays,
Shoot round the expansion, noon's excessive blaze,
Confine the empire of surrounding night,
And reign, and glory, in immortal light.
For know, blessed favorite, suns are those fair flames;
Worlds round them roll, and day perpetual beams:
Those worlds unnumber'd circling moons adorn,
And with long splendors comets mid them burn.
As in the world of minds, with golden chain,
Attractive Love extends her blissful reign,
In one pure realm all sainted beings joins,
GOD with his sons, his sons with GOD combines:
The bond to all of pure perfection given,
The life, the beauty, peace, and joy of heaven:
So this stupendous frame, by him alone
Who calls their names, supported, numbered, known,
These countless systems in one system joined,
Their size, their distance, with nice art designed,
A great, attracting power, on all impressed,
Connects, moves, governs, and forbids to rest.
By this great power, impelling and impelled,
All worlds move on through space' unmeasured field.
Around their planets moons refulgent stray;
Around their suns those planets trace their way;
Around your central heaven all systems roll;
And one great circling motion rules the whole.
O scene divine, on those bright towers to stand,
And mark the wonders of the Eternal hand;
To see through space unnumber'd systems driven,
Worlds round their suns, and suns around the heaven;
To see one ordinance worlds and suns obey;
Their order, peace, and fair, harmonious way;
Their solemn silence: varying pomp divine;
Their fair proportions, and their endless shine!
Some nearer rolling in celestial light;
Some distant glimmering towered the bordering night;
'Till far removed from thought the regions lie,
Where angels never winged the lonely, verging sky,
On the clear glass as smiles the beauteous form,
And youth's fair light, and eyes of glory, charm;
As lucid streams, with face serene, unfold
Spring's gayest prime, and flowers that bloom in gold;
As boundless ocean's smooth, resplendent plain
Rebeams the skies, and all their wondrous train,
No part, no wave, but feels the sun's broad ray,
And glows, reflective, with surrounding day:
So round the immense, on fair creation's breast,
In endless pomp ^he GODHEAD shines impressed;
His love, his be^uty, over all nature burns;
Each sun unfolds it, and each world returns;
Each day, each hour, the glory bright improves.
And GOD, with ceaseless smile, the immortal image loves.
Winged with pure flame through space' unmeasured rounds,
Thy soul shall visit being's farthest bounds;
When orbs begin, instruct their mass to roll;
For changing seasons fix a steady pole;
Teach eve to purple, golden morn to rise,
And light new suns in solitary skies.
Upborne from world to world, shall thou behold
How ever-varying wonders GOD unfold;
In each new realm, with growing bliss pursue
Scenes unimagin'd, nations ever new;
See some through highborn virtues swiftly soar,
Some humbler duties, humbler thoughts explore;
To every race, new thoughts new senses bring;
On every plain, new vegetations spring;
Over virtue's sons eternal morning bloom;
Over guilt's vile throngs ascend eternal gloom;
Over mingled nations mingling seasons roll,
And peace, and tumult, wrap the changing pole.
To endless years, thy mind, inspired, shall rise
Through knowledge, love, and beauty, of the skies;
To heights angelic, archangelic, soar,
'Till man's faint language paint the heights no more*
When borne to glory, winged to slights supreme,
Thy soul shall reach creation's first extreme,
Beyond all thought assume her last abode,
And seek the bosom of the involving GOD.
The Vision ceased. At once the scenes decayed,
His bright form vanished and his glories fled:
Swift to the camp the exulting Chief returned,
While the glad day star in the orient burned.
THE CONQUEST OF CANAAN: BOOK XI.

ARGUMENT.
Morning* Hareshah returns to Gibeon. Army assembles. Speech of Caleb. Hanniel.
Joshua's advice to him; his reply. Joshua's prayer. Cloud rolls before the army
toward Gibeon. Prospect of the Heathen host beyond the city. Speech of Joshua
on that occasion. Israelites descend from the mountain. Jabin prepares for
battle, and arranges the heathen army on the bank of a small river. Gibeonites
ascend the walls to view the battle. Aradon marches his troops out to meet
Joshua, who gives the command of them to Almiran. Arrangement of the
combatants. Joshua by a stratagem draws the Heathens from their advantageous
post. General engagement. Joshua's exploits. He kills Medan and Talmon. Zedeck
rallies the heathens; but is forced down the bank, and killed. Egon. Joshua,
seeing Hazor strongly posted on the bank, moves down the river, and rescues
Almiran, kills Piram, and routs Jarmuth. Japhia. Exploits of Zimri. He kills
Hoham, and puts Hebron into confusion. Jabin rallies them, and kills Hanniel.
Asher retires. Joshua leaves his division to engage Hazor; and rallies Asher.
Combat between him and Jabin. Heathens routed. Storm of Hail. Israelites return
to their camp and are met by their wives and children singing praise to the
Creator* Conclusion.

THE CONQUEST OF CANAAN. BOOK XI.
NOW rose in heaven the great, the final day,
Where fates of chiefs, and kings, and kingdoms lay
Morn dressed in golden pride the cliffs on high,
Streamed over the groves, and brightened round the sky:
No cloud, no mist, obscured the blue serene;
And peace, and silence, hushed the solemn scene.
To Caleb's tent alert the Hero strode,
And roused Hareshah to the field of blood. --
With active haste to Gibeon's prince repair;
To range his thousands be his instant care:
Ere the glad sun climb half the etherial main,
Shall Heaven's broad standard tremble on the plain. --
Far over the western field, with keen delight,
He winged his course, and vanished from the sight.
And now once more the clarion's dreadful sound
Inspires to arms, and shakes the banner'd ground:
To arms the martial thousands raptured spring;
Their songs resound, their clashing bucklers ring:
Rolled on the winds, imperial ensigns play,
And waved their splendors to the bursting day.
Now joined in marshalled ranks the generous train,
And gloomy columns darkened over the plain;
When, robbed in white, their hoary fathers came,
Great in past fields, and heirs of deathless fame.
One was their voice, and from their reverend eyes,
The bold heroic flame began to rise;
The soul stood struggling in the heaving breast,
And every limb their vigorous thoughts expressed.
When Caleb thus -- The great concluding day
Now calls to arms, and Heaven directs the way:
What though unnumber'd hosts against us rise,
And with proud madness brave insulted Skies;
Shall cumbrous throngs the meanest arm dismay?
Or one base thought distain the glorious day?
Think how bold Abraham swept the midnight plain,
While realms opposed, and millions fought, in vain;
How two brave patriarchs, in one friendly gloom,
Sank Shechem's towers and opened a nation's tomb;
Think how these fires for yon unbroken toiled,
Dared the rough main, and proved the hideous wild;
Made spiry towns, and haughty kings a prey,
And forced over countless lands resistless way.
See your fond partners in sad grief arrayed,
Behold your children claim parental aid!
Your hands their freedom and their fate suspend;
Your swords must conquer, or your race must end.
Nor let these narrow scenes your thoughts confine;
Claim nobler views and pass the selfish line.
Ages unborn from yon shall trace their doom,
Heaven's future Seers, and heroes yet to come;
If slaves, or men, this day your hands decide,
The scorn of nations, or the world's great pride:
Empire and bondage in your bosoms lie;
It Is yours to triumph, or it is ours to die.
He spoke, and silent to the all-bounteous Skies
Stretched wide his hands, and raised his kindling eyes:
Each glowing visage flashed disdain around
And hoarse applauses shook the neighboring ground.
Bright from the lucid main, the sun's broad eye
Looked in imperial splendour from the sky;
With war's gay pomp then shone the embattled plains;
In proud battalions rose the martial trains;
A broken radiance burst from trembling shields,
And haughty heroes stalked along the fields.
Bold Hanniel there in shining armor stood,
And hoped a deathless name in scenes of blood*
He saw the host to final combat rise,
The champions nations, and a realm the prize.
Now wealth allured; the rival now alarmed;
Strong pride impelled, and splendid conquest charmed;
His wounds, his pains, in quick oblivion gone,
The wish of glory prompts the warrior on;
Pleased, his fond fancy flies from silent shame
To plains of triumph, and to wreaths of fame.
Him Joshua viewed with pity in his breast,
And kindly thus the haughty chief addressed --
If, when dread war resounds her hoarse alarm,
Health flush the cheek, and vigor brace the arm,
To fight, the warrior virtue fame command,
And knaves alone refuse the needed hand.
But thou, brave Hanniel, seek'st the field in vain,
Pale with lost blood, and weak with ceaseless pain*
Unstrung to fight, and impotent to ^ly,
Useless, alive; nor glorious, should thou die.
In fields of frequent strife thy garlands bloom*
Let not their verdure wither on thy tomb:
No feeble aid such numerous honors claim,
Nor can base envy crop the growing fame.
He spoke, impatient Hanniel quick returned,
And keen resentment in his visage burned --
While yon bright orb rolls on the mighty doom
Of millions born, and millions yet to come,
What chief, what man, who boasts a reasoning mind,
Will hide in shame, or sleep in tents confined?
Let these, if Jacob's race such culprits knows,
Shirnk from great scenes, and die in vile repose,
^
^
Where clarions roar my (...)
Glue to the fight, and ask no str^ng^h (...)
Unbroke by wounds, my voice shall now inspire
The coward's languor, and the warrior's fire;
This shield, or these frail limbs, well pleased, arrest
The lance, that flies to wound a worthier breast.
But Hanniel's glory why should Joshua fear?
Do rival names alarm thy tender ear?
On yon broad plain unnumber'd stars arise,
Move in gay ranks, and triumph round the skies;
Each lends his beam to swell the pomp divine,
Nor grieves that neighboring spangles brighter shine.
How beauteous thus in Honor's Angel-race,
When some blessed era numerous heroes grace,
Mean self disdained, if virtuous all engage
To fill with light the constellated age.
Some shining deed should this right hand atchieve,
Unstained, unrivaled, Joshua's name would live;
Then wish no more my days consumed in shame;
Nor grudge the glory, generous actions claim.
The Leader heard, and wished that Heaven had joined
A heart more honest with so bright a mind:
Through his great bosom thrilled a sudden pain,
Where sweet compassion mixed with brave disdain.
Sighing he said -- How blind is reason's eye,
When Heaven ordains o'er-weening man to die!
Now through the host he cast a piercing view,
And every rank, and every station, knew;
Then, while mute silence hushed the adoring bands,
From a tall rock, he reared his suppliant hands. --
O thou, whose throne, uprais'd beyond all height,
Glows in the effulgence of unutter'd light,
Over earth, over hell, over heaven, extends thy sway;
Angels, Archangels, Thrones, and Powers obey;
All scenes, all worlds, confess thy hand divine,
And seas, and skies, and stars, and suns, are thine.
At thy command, to glory nations rise;
At thy command, each guilty kingdom dies;
At thy command, awakes the trumpet's roar:
Death walks the plain, and earth is drenched in gore:
Hushed by thy sovereign nod, the tempests cease;
Peace is thy choice, and all the world is peace.
This day, O Power supreme! against the skies,
Sheathed in dread arms, unnumber'd thousands rise.
As raging flames the shaggy mountains burn,
The groves to dust, and fields to deserts turn;
So let thy vengeance sweep the embattled plain,
And teach proud monarchs GOD'S eternal reign.
From endless years thy all-encircling mind
To Abraham's race this beauteous land assigned:
The land, where Truth shall fix her lasting seat;
Where sky-born Virtue seeks a calm retreat;
Where blessed Redemption opes her living morn;
Where heaven commences, and where GOD is born.
For this thy voice the sacred promise gave;
For this thy thunders cleft the Egyptian wave;
Rich manna shower'd; with streams the desert smiled,
And the whole heaven descended on the wild.
Still, O unchanging Mind! thy bounty shower;
Draw thy red sword, and stretch thine arm of power.
To gain these realms, the crown of long desire,
Let Heaven protect us, and let Heaven inspire!
He spoke: a rushing voice began to roar,
Like caverns, echoing on the sea-beat shore;
Deep rang the hollow sound: and over the train,
The cloud stupendous sailed along the plain;
Broad flames, in fierce effusion, round it played,
Scorched the green fields, and brightened all the shade:
Towered western hills the fearful gloom retired,
And all the splendour in one flash expired.
Loud rose the trump; and ranged in dread array,
Behind the cloud the squadrons traced their way;
The burnished helm, blue mail, and upright spear,
Gleam'd over the plain, and starr'd the kindled air:
High strode the Leader in the glorious van,
And round his arms an awful glory ran:
For GOD enrob'd him with a pomp divine,
And bade an angel in his countenance shine.
Thus, when no cloud obscures the autumnal even,
And night's dark hand unveils the vault of heaven,
Crowned with pure beams, her sons in beauty rise,
And glow, and sparkle, over unmeasured skies;
The moon, bright regent, leads the immortal train,
And walks in pride imperial round the plain.
Now climbed the bands the mountain's towering height,
And over the subject region cast their sight;
There glister'd Gibeon's domes in trembling fires,
And all the grandeur of a thousand spires.
Beyond her walls, a far-extended plain
Spread, like the surface of the steeping main:
A mighty host there left the bounded eye,
And lost its distant terrors in the sky.
Full in the effulgence of the morn's broad beam,
Stretched the tremendous front, a ridge of flame,
Of length immeasurable. Either wide
Waved with a thousand nations' banner'd pride;
Tossed in gay triumph, lucid ensigns shone,
And cast their various splendour on the sun:
Swift round the region dim-seen chariots rolled;
The far steeds bounded wrapped in twinkling gold*
With spears and helms adorned of countless trains,
Rose the full pomp of constellated plains;
And proud with wanton beams, the sun-bright shields
Joined like unnumber'd moons, and dazzled all the fields*
Unmoved, great Joshua round him cast his eyes.
And saw the interminable legions rise:
Then thus, while Israel hushed in silence stood,
Ranged in just ranks, and faced the field of blood.
Behold, on yon bright plain, embodied stands
The gathered force of all Canaan's lands!
Gathered by Heaven's right hand, and sad despa^^,
To crown our arms, and sink in one dread war!
Hail my brave sons, with me, the immortal day,
That opes to blissful peace the glorious way,
The hour, long numbered in impatient skies,
The morn, ordained with every pomp to rise,
By angels watched, by Heaven's dread signs led on,
Sinai's fierce flames, and Jordan's walls of stone.
Each boundless hope let yon fair field inspire;
Each warrior kindle with a leader's fire:
The spoils of kingdoms each rapt eye behold;
Ensigns of fame, and shields of moony gold;
The herds, that wanton round a thousand rills;
The flocks, that whiten on a thousand hills;
The corn, all verdant over unmeasured plains;
The world, where spring with smiling plenty reigns;
Where olives swell; where beauteous figs refine;
And warm, and purpling, glows the clustered vine.
This day ordains them ours: this mighty day
Through realms unknown shall stretch our potent sway;
Far as the hills, where suns begin to rise;
Far as the seas, that limit evening skies;
Till fading years unloose the sleeping grave,
And time's last current joins the eternal wave.
There too, my sons, shall boundless glory rise,
And yon bright field of conquest fill the skies.
Through Israel's future tribes the tale shall ring;
The sage record it, and the prophet sing;
Our deeds, our honors, wake the slumbering lyre;
Warm the saint's praise, and wake the hero's fire;
^ous'd by the theme, new arts of virtue grow;
New chiefs break forth, and rival wonders flow;
Truth's happy sons rehearse in raptured strains,
Far through all climes, and ages, Gibeon's plains;
To morn's etherial host new bliss be given,
And human triumphs tune the harps of heaven.
For know, when darkness last involved the skies,
I saw the promised land in vision rise.
I saw sweet peace exalted joys unfold;
Fair towers ascend, and temples beam in gold;
Kings, sprung from Jacob's lineage, mount the throne,
And stretch their sway to years and realms unknown;
Art raise her scepter; wisdom's light revive,
And angel Virtue bid our glory live.
I saw Messiah bright from heaven descend,
And spread his sway to earth's remotest end;
Deep Gentile darkness yield to light refined;
And truth, and virtue, flow to all mankind.
I saw the world, where Powers and Seraphs bright
Shine in pure robes, and rove in endless light;
Where, in new youth, the patriarchs, from their thrones
Hail a long starry train of heavenly sons;
Where Abraham's steps his native skies sustain,
And Moses raptured meets his GOD again.
On you, my sons, these mighty scenes suspend;
From you shall Israel's fame and bliss descend;
From you shall princes, heroes, prophets spring;
From you be born the heaven-appointed king;
On this great day his earthly kingdom stand,
Reach through all times, and flow to every land;
To bliss, in distant ages, nations rise,
The world ennoble, and expand the skies:
Rush then to glory; GOD'S tremendous arm
Moves in the flaming front, and guides us to the storm.
He spoke: a shout convulsed the mountain's brow,
And burst sonorous over the world below:
Each warrior on the plain in fancy stood,
Drove back whole hosts, and ruled the scenes of blood;
Each on his falchion cast a frequent eye,
And thought it bliss, in Israel's cause to die.
As sullen clouds, when blasts in silence rest,
Hang black and heavy on the mountain's breast;
Slow sink the volumes down its hoary side,
Shroud all the cliffs, and roll in gloomy pride:
At once the winds arise; and sounding rain
Pours with impetuous fury over the plain:
So the dark hosts descend in deep array,
And over the champaign drive their dreadful way.
From the far plains, great Jabin's eye beheld
The squadrons, thickening on the distant field.
For when from Joshua's arm his host retired,
Stung by disgrace, with fierce resentment fired,
Some future fight his angry thoughts designed,
To glut the vengeance of his haughty mind.
To Gibeon's fields he steers his sullen course,
Where circling kings combined their gathered force;
Chiefs rushed to conquest from a thousand lands,
Whirled all their cars, and led their countless bands.
To guide their strength against their dreaded foes
All with one voice the mighty hero chose.
He, pleased once more to rule the dreadful plain,
Surveyed the terrors of the unnumber'd train;
Surveyed a host, beyond his wishes great,
And asked the gods to give no happier fate.
In splendid arms confessed to dreadful view,
To final fight, to final fame, he drew;
Full on his shield, with various forms enrolled,
OR DEATH, OR CONQUEST -- blazed in words of gold.
In fields far west, a torrent, with rough waves,
The rocky shore with endless fury laves.
Here, over the stream high banks majestic hung,
And with sad murmurs hollow caverns rung;
There, for the squadrons, rushing to the affray,
Smooth, sloping shores prepared an easy way.
High on the western margin of the flood,
A wall of fire, Canaan's millions stood.
Here Jabin's will ordained his host to stay,
Shields joined with shields, and wedged in firm array.
For well he knew, when Israel's rushing force
Up the rough bank should urge their toilsome course,
Their broken ranks would fall an easy prey,
And fame, and triumph, close the important day.
Now Israel's host, slow-moving over the plain,
Successive rolled, as waves disturb the main;
In every face a fixed, calm bravery shined;
And not a hero cast a look behind.
High on her ramparts Gibeon's children rose,
Surveyed the fields, and eyed the impending foes.
Here in fond arms, the tender Mother bare
The babe, sweet offspring of her anxious care,
Hung over its infant charms, and joy'd to trace
The sire's loved image in its blooming face:
Then on the combat turned a boding view,
Wrung her white hands, and shed the glistening dew.
Here the gay Child, with pleased, and wondering eye,
Caught the broad standard, streaming in the sky;
On the red armor cast a raptured gaze,
And raised his artless hands, and marked the splendid blaze.
Here, bathed in tears, and whelmed with timorous care,
In woe more lovely, mourned the melting Fair*
Over Gibeon's host their eyes incessant roved,
And each, mid thousands, traced the youth she loved:
Fond hope, ere eve gave champions to his steel,
And at her feet his shining garlands fell.
Then fear presents him weltering on the plain,
Soft, healing, female aid implored in vain;
Closed were those eyes, that beamed etherial fire,
Glowed with young joy, or languish'd sweet desire,
Dumb was the voice, that every wish could move,
And cold the form, that waked unutter'd love.
Here hoary Age in newborn pleasure stood,
And war's dread glories fired his languid blood;
Long-buried years rushed forward to the view;
What hosts they battled, and what chiefs they slew:
Each on his brethren gazed with glad surprise,
And the great soul stood kindling in their eyes.
From northern gates her dark battalions poured,
And many a hero fierce to combat tower'd;
His warlike thousands wise Aradon led,
The white locks trembling over his ancient head.
Hail, mighty Chief! -- the hoary prince began --
Favorite of GOD, and virtuous friend of man!
Blessed be thy steps, that bring this kind relief
To feeble age, and solitary grief.
In fields of conflict once rejoiced I stood,
With death familiar, and with scenes of blood.
But now sad age my head has whitened over;
This palsied arm must wield the sword no more.
To mourn, to weep is all my future doom,
Drawn near to death, and bending over the tomb*
These bands thy voice obey; in danger's field
Their manly bosoms never knew to yield:
Nor will their feet, long tried in honor's race,
Now learn to flee, and first commence disgrace.
But, fixed to death, their king, their land to save,
All force will hazard, and all terrors brave.
When round the host I turn my weeping eyes,
And gaze, and gaze, my soul, with anguish, cries
Where, where is Elam? Oh, may no sad doom
Compel thee to a son's untimely tomb!
A happier life, a brighter lot be thine;
Taste all the rapturing joys that once were mine.
From childless age may Heaven his chosen save,
Nor bring thy hoary hairs in sorrow to the grave!
Great prince! the Chief, with cheering voice, replied --
Thy nation's father, and thy country's pride!
Not singly thou the pangs of grief have known;
I mourn a daughter, as thou weep'st a son.
From hearts too fond, Heaven called the pair away
To fields of bliss, and climes of lasting day.
May every virtue in thy breast refine,
Till those fair climes, and all that bliss be thine.
But now retire, where yon bright chariot stands;
Let youth and vigor lead thy warlike bands,
For see^ to fight Canaan's millions rise!
And ^ark, what clamors rend the boundless skies!
The king obeyed. In arms, the ardent throng,
Behind Almiran, darkly rushed along;
Almiran* Gibeon's noblest* bravest son,
Led the bold heroes, and like lightning shone.
In three vast squadrons stood the heathens strength,
And rose a mighty front of dreadful length.
Over ^^rthern banks, where chariots hoarsely rung,
(...) clouds of thunder, haughty Hebron hung:
There too fierce Eglon rushed with dreadful roar,
Like the long murmurs of the sounding shore.
Nor feebler legions fill the southern plain;
There Lachish, Jarmuth there, the fight sustain;
To the dire center numerous nations throng,
And Jabin guides the storm, and swiftly flames along.
With piercing eyes the Chief his foes descried,
And bade his host in three vast squares divide.
Against Lachish Gibeon rolls in proud array;
Against Hebron Asher bends a dreadful way:
A fires pursue a comet's sanguine form,
Behind great Joshua drives the central storm.
Now over the plain, as ocean pours his tide,
Their streaming ensigns reared in purple pride,
Far north, and southward stretched the chosen train,
And crossed in gloomy pomp the dreadful plain.
Near, and more near, the undaunted warriors drew;
For well the Chief, by sure experience knew
That nations, taught in sudden fight to rise,
To war by stealth, and triumph by surprise,
To wiles, vainglorious, fall an easy prey,
(...), thronged in tumult wild, are swept away.
Thence, near the foe he bade the squadrons move,
Tempt with keen taunts, and with proud threatenings prove,
That chiefs, and men, with childish rage overcome,
Might quit the shore, and haste to certain doom.
Now near the stream the sacred thousands stood,
Their breasts all panting for the scenes of blood.
At once, as some black storm begins to rise,
A cloud of arrows filled the western skies;
The long, ascending gloom all heaven overspread,
And the fields darkened with a transient shade.
Then stones on stones tempestuous either poured:
And darts on darts in quick succession shower'd:
Now here, now there, expiring warriors fell,
And shrill beneath them rung the clashing steel.
At once, as moved by fear, the Chief withdrew,
And bade his host the distant walls pursue.
With joy, the heathens eyed their backward way,
Raised a long shout, and sprang to seize the prey.
Swift rushed the exulting thousands down the shore;
For ranks behind, urged on the ranks before;
Loud ring the chariots, swift the coursers bound,
And a deep thunder waves along the ground.
Around, great Jabin cast a mournful view,
And saw his foes retreat, his friends pursue,
His laws contemned, that bade the thousands stay,
Till over the torrent Israel urged their way;
Kenn'd the deep snare, by Joshua wisely laid,
And to himself with sighs thus fiercely said. --
I see, proud chief, I see thy prosperous wiles;
On me fate frowns; on thee propitious smiles*
But not alone I prove the general doom;
Ten thousand ghosts shall meet me at the tomb:
Avenged, and happy to the shades I Will go,
To bid thy princes quake in realms below.
Thus spoke the king, and deemed his ruin nigh,
A fearful vengeance reddening in his eye;
Strong, fell despair inflamed his eager look;
His bands gazed trembling, and his princes shook.
Meantime with smiles the sacred Chief beheld
His foes rush headlong over the embattled field:
At once his piercing voice restrained the flight,
Wheeled his long ranks, and marshalled to the fight.
At once the trump's tremendous blast ascends
The plains all shudder, and the concave rends;
Loud as the storm's ten thousand thunders rise,
A shout unmeasured rocks the lands and skies;
Again high heaven is gloom'd with stony showers;
Again all either darts unnumber'd pours;
With deep convulsion roars the closing war;
Fierce bounds the steed; sonorous rolls the car;
With one broad ruin heaves the earth amain,
And Night, and Death, and Horror, shroud the plain.
So pours a storm on Greenland's frozen shore;
The hoarse winds rage; the maddening billows roar;
When boundless darkness wraps the realms on high,
And flaming meteors stream across the sky:
Huge isles of raging ice, together driven,
With bursting thunder rend air, sea, and heaven:
Rocks rise over rocks; over mountains mountains roll,
And the world trembles to the distant pole.
Thus over the field the dreadful tumult grows;
Alike impetuous, foes encounter foes;
Where Asher's sons proud Hebron's host engage;
Or where bold Gibeon pours her torrent rage;
Or where, around the Chief, immingled rise
Triumphant clamours, and expiring cries.
Long roared the tumult of the dubious fight,
And no base coward wished inglorious flight:
All fierce to combat rushed the undaunted train;
Nor these the palm would lose, nor those could gain;
Till clothed in terror, Joshua's dreadful arm
Began the triumph, and led on the storm.
Two chiefs, whose silver arms confessed their sway,
Raised their broad buklers in his fateful way.
By their fair wives a common fire they claimed;
And Medan this, and Talmon that, was named*
Of royal race, from Salem's wall they came,
Their deeds just budding in the field of fame.
Cleft through the side brave Medan gasping fell;
And Talmon trembling fled the lifted steel.
By his own friends a javelin swiftly hurled
Plunged his freed spirit to the nether world;
Far round the field a shout of joy ascends,
And groans re-murmur from his sadden'd friends.
Then swift the Hero wheeled his flaming sword;
Like mountain streams his host behind him poured;
Loud roared the thunders of the dreadful plain,
Rocked the tall groves, and filled the etherial main:
Increasing horror rent the world around,
And steeds, and cars, and warriors mingled on the ground.
Now near the stream approached the sounding war,
When fierce to combat rolled a splendid car;
There giant Zedeck rose in dreadful view;
Two furious steeds the mighty monarch drew;
With wild impetuous rage, they foamed along,
And, pale before them, fled the parting throng.
From Joshua's course he saw his bands retire;
His reddening aspect flashed a gloomy fire;
With huge, hoarse voice the furious hero cried,
While the plains murmured, and the groves replied,
Whatever wretch from this bright combat flies,
By the just gods, the impious dastard dies.
Nor hope to 'scape the keen, avenging blade
In the still cot, or in the lonely shade.
Soon shall this sword, with victory crowned, return;
And wrath, and vengeance, all your dwellings burn;
Your bodies, limb from limb, this arm shall tear,
Nor sons, nor wives, nor fires, nor infants, spare;
But bid the hungry hawks your race devour,
And call grim wolves to feast in floods of gore.
He spoke; astonished, some more nimbly flew;
And some to conflict with fresh ardour drew:
Despair once more the growing flight repelled,
And gave new horrors to the gloomy field.
Meantime on Joshua drove the sounding car,
And burst impetuous through the thickest war,
Rough, heavy, dreadful, by the giant thrown
Flew the vast fragment of a craggy stone;
Scarce 'scap'd the wary Chief, with sudden bound,
While the broad ruin plowed the crumbling ground.
A javelin then the monarch's hand impelled,
That sung, and trembled, against the Hero's shield;
Swift over his head a second hissing flies,
And a pierced warrior groans, and falls, and dies.
At once great Joshua raised his reeking sword,
And with deep wounds the maddening coursers gored;
Through cleaving ranks the coursers backward flew,
And swift from fight the helpless monarch drew.
To the high shore, impendent over the flood,
They rushed, as whirlwinds sweep the rending wood;
To turn they tried, with short and sudden wheel;
But tried in vain; the sounding chariot fell.
Prone down the lofty bank the steeds pursued,
Where sharp, and ragged rocks beneath were strewn;
All shrill the giant's striking mail resounds:
With clattering crash, the cracking car rebounds;
White over his lifeless head the waters roar --
Lost in the stream, and doomed to rise no more. --
As, when the south's fierce blasts the main deform,
And ^oll the pealful onset of the storm;
Hung are the heavens with night; the world around*
Deep-murmuring, trembles to the solemn sound;
Full on dread Longa's wild-resounding shore
Hills, waved over hills, ascend, and burst, and roar:
Safe in his cot, the hoary sailor hears,
Or drops, for fancied wrecks, unbidden tears.
A boundless shout, from Israel's raptured train,
Rent the broad skies, and shook the dreadful plain.
For now, their champion, trust, and glory lost,
From Joshua's vengeance flew sad Salem's host;
Before him naught availed the shields, and spears,
But chiefs, and foaming steeds, and rattling cars,
Ranks urging ranks, squadrons over squadrons borne,
Down the bank plunged; the bank behind them torn,
Sunk with a rushing sound: great Joshua's arm
Uplifted, imminent impelled the storm.
Alert, he bounded on the yielding sand,
And scattered ruin from his red right hand.
The white waves foamed around his midway side,
As fierce he thundered through the rushing tide.
Two blooming youths, he dashed against the rock,
Where Zedeck's chariot felt the fatal shock;
Their gushing blood ran purple through the wave,
And thousands with them found a watery grave.
There, mid vile throngs, to untimely fate a prey,
Young, generous Egon breathed his soul away.
Him Salem's nymphs resounded through the vales,
Or sung melodious, to responsive gales.
He, from the mountain wilds, and cliffs sublime,
Untrod, uncultur'd, from the first of time,
Drove the fierce beasts, by arms and arts compelled,
To seek their safety in the lowland field.
By flames unclos'd, by hounds and swains pursued,
They fled each fastness of the impervious wood;
Ambush'd, in vales beneath the savage prey
Rushed on the spear, and yell'd their lives away.
Then howling wilds the traveller ceased to appall;
Then night spread harmless round the unguarded stall
His flocks, the rising swain with joy surveyed,
And slaughtered lambs defiled no more the glade.
Egon, each pipe, each voice of music sung;
And Egon's glory courts and caverns rung:
But passed was all his fame; by Joshua's hand
Plunged in the stream, and choked with surging sand,
While from the bank the warriors leaped amain,
Crushed, drowned, he mingled with the numerous slain.
On the steep, western bank all Hazor stood:
A cloud of fire, high-towering over the flood:
Their darts unnumber'd Israel's host invade,
And many an eye is closed in death's dark shade.
Swift down the shore a rock with fury fell,
And crushed two warriors, wrapped in shining steel:
Near Joshua's steps the craggy ruin poured;
The Hero sprang; the foaming torrent roared.
Then stones on stones, with sounding tempest driven,
Filled the wide concave of the troubled heaven:
Beneath their shields the prudent warriors stood;
All either rang and foamed the reddening flood;
'Till mighty Joshua, breathing wide dismay,
Swift down the raging torrent drove his way.
Where southward waves, expanding ceased to roar,
The stream was bounded by a sloping shore.
Hither the hero bent his awful course;
His host behind him poured their mighty force;
Pierce up the shore he rushed; a dreadful band
Thronged round their chief, and darkened all the strand*
Here brave Almi^an, like a sweeping fire,
Urged his dread path, and bade his soes expire.
Tall in the gloomy van* the hero sped,
And Lachish pale before him fell or ^led:
Such fiery terrors round his visage glowed;
Such streams of slaughter from his falchion flowed.
'Till, generous youth, an arrow found thy side,
And down thy armor gushed the living tid^.
Thy sire had grasped his long-neglected shield,
And followed, trembling, to the deathful field:
There on thy deeds he cast an anxious view;
There touched with transport, felt his youth renew;
Then saw thee falling, pale, deprived of breath,
Plunged on the foe, and sunk in whelming death.
The youth, great Joshua caught in friendly arms,
His shield averting war's impendent harms;
Chafed by his hand, again he opened his eyes;
His lips respir'd; his bloom began to rise.
Then Gibeon's sons the mighty Leader fired,
And sorrow prompted, and revenge inspired.
Now dressed in golden pride, to crimson war,
Tall, beauteous Piram drove his shining car.
Born in the stillness of a court serene,
Where peace, and pleasure led the jocund scene,
He loathed dire fight, to gentler thoughts inclined;
And love, and music, charmed his feeling mind.
Soft pity touched his heart; and often a tear
He dropped, and mourned the human doom severe;
The unnumber'd ills of wasting pride would rue,
And wish that kings the sweets of friendship knew.
Yet, not of servile kind, his thoughts had soared,
In brighter days, and Art's fair realms explored.
Such was his soul, as grace from heaven refined
Can warm, and ripen, to an angel's mind.
To combat now the prince reluctant rode,
When full before him Israel's Leader stood.
Pleased, he beheld the graceful form ascend,
And wished the gods had made the Chief his friend.
But vain his wishes; by the Hero thrown,
Full on his forehead bursts a sounding stone,
He fell; his coursers backward rushed amain
And snatched the monarch over the cloudy plain.
His hapless fall pale Jarmuth's sons beheld*
Grief froze their hearts, and fear their nerves congealed
The Chief pursues; their trembling bands retire;
Deep groans ascend, and troops on troops expire*
Wide rolls the dust; the skies are snatched from sight,
And death hangs dreadful over the growing fight*
There, throned in state, and dressed in burnished steel,
Lachish' fair prince, Japhia, hapless fell.
He bade soft songs awake the trembling lyre,
With notes of magic, and with words of fire;
Such songs, as Moses, uninspir'd, might sing;
Like him, a bard, a hero, and a king.
But far beyond the pride of pomp, and power,
He loved the realms of nature to explore;
With lingering gaze, Edenian spring surveyed;
Morn's fairy splendors, night's gay curtain'd shade;
The high hoar cliff; the grove's benighting gloom;
The wild rose, widowed, over the mouldering tomb;
The heaven-embosom'd sun; the rainbow's die,
Where lucid forms disport to fancy's eye.
When roused to war, and deeds of deathless name,
Faint shone to him the charms of martial fame:
But fired to ecstacy* his soul beheld
The stormy grandeur of the troubled field:
The morn, that trembles over the steel-bright plains;
The whirlwind car, winged steed, and clashing trains.
Such scenes the warrior sung. The swains around
Hung on the enchantment of the wildering sound:
Soft over the lyre the voice of music passed,
Wild as the woodland warblings of the waste*
Each savage softened, as the numbers rose,
Forsook his falchion, and forgot his foes.
As dread before him glowed the Hero's face,
His angel pomp, and heaven-descended grace;
He stopped; he gazed; and with fond fancy warm,
Glued to the solemn glories of his form;
Swift through his bosom drove the deadly spear,
And all his beauteous dreams dissolved in air.
Meantime far north the sons of Asher poured,
And fierce to combat chiefs and heroes tow^r'd:
There, like a whirlwind, rapid Zimri flew,
And, like a tempest, countless ^ands pursue:
Clouds after clouds behind him darkly roll,
And shouts of glory heave the murmuring pole*
As when two seas, by winds together hurled,
With bursting fury shake the solid world;
Waves pil'd over waves, the watery mountains rise,
And foam, and roar, and rage, against the skies:
So joined the combat; ranks, over ranks impelled,
Swelled the hoarse tumult of the hideous field;
Black drifts of dust becloud the gloomy ground;
Hoarse groans ascend, and clashing arms resound.
And now, where Zimri broke the embodied war,
Imperious Hoham drove his sounding car;
Like flames, his rapid courses rushed along,
Forced a red path, and crushed the thickening throng:
His hissing lances shower'd destruction round,
And streaming bodies strewn the crimson ground.
With joy, bold Zimri kenn'd the prince afar
And winged his javelin through the flashing air;
Deep in his throat was lodged the avenging steel;
With groans, the monarch panting, struggling, fell:
The sword indignant gash'd his cleaving side,
Freed the pale ghost, and poured the vital tide.
With shouts of triumph swelled the etherial main,
And new convulsions shook the stormy plain.
The cars rushed backward; foaming coursers bound*
The shrill swords clash, and hollow groans resound.
'Twixt the long banks remurmuring clamors roar*
And eyes unnumber'd wish the farthest shore.
As, swelled with rains, the autumnal stream ascends,
Foams over the rocks, and all the mountain rends,
Heaved deep, with groans the uprooted forest yields,
And huge, unwieldy oaks, plunge cumbrous to the fields;
So furious Asher, with resistless sway,
On Hebron bursting broke a dreadful way;
Swift over the floods the warriors eager fly,
And steeds, and men, on earth immingled lie.
On these dire scenes great Jabin cast his view,
And saw his friends retire, his foes pursue,
Then, while the storm of war brave Zedeck bore,
He whirled his chariot down the western shore.
As, stained with blood, a meteor's midnight beam
Cleaves the dun clouds, and trails a length of flame;
At once, with dreadful burst, its terrors fly,
And a deep thunder rocks the shuddering sky:
(...)* throned tremendous in his sun-bright car,
Rushed the impetuous Hero to the war;
Loud to their ears his voice terrific came,
And his fierce eyeballs flashed a withering flame --
Rouse, rouse to fight, to triumph bend your way;
Nor yield these slaves the wished immortal day.
Shall Hebron's sons, that never knew to fly,
Now turn inglorious, and like dastards die?
Let all your ancient deeds each soul inspire,
And each bold warrior emulate his fire.
This hour propitious brings the glorious doom,
And sweeps these wretches to the coward's tomb.
He spoke, and furious, with resistless force
Burst on his foes and stopped their eager course:
All Hebron round him swift to conflict turned,
New life informed them, and new bravery burned;
Squadrons on squadrons wedged their deep array,
And darker horrors gloom'd the dreadful day.
Him Hanniel saw; for here in fiercest fight
With joy he mingled, and disdained base flight.
No griding anguish now his limb distressed;
No thought, but glory, triumphed in his breast*
Chiefs to his arm had given the parting breath,
And vulgar warriors stained his sword with death.
Alive, impetuous, burned the martial flame,
And every hope beat high for endless fame.
On Jabin's car the undaunted warrior ^lew:
The car, like whirlwinds near him swiftly drew.
This the blessed hour the hero deemed to gain
The garland, wished so long, but wished in vain.
The Chief of foes his raptured eye surveyed,
The destined victim of his conquering blade.
No fear disturbed, lest combat's fickle doom
Should change the lot, and open another's tomb:
He smiled, from Joshua sure the palm to win,
And felt fresh honors round his temples twine.
At once, by Jabin's hand like lightening driven,
A spear flew nimbly through the dusty heaven;
Deep in his forehead sunk the unerring steel:
Without a groan the haughty warrior fell:
No soul more restless ever from earth retired,
Nor pride more boundless ever in dust expired.
As, when bold youths, the mount's dim summit gained,
Upheave the huge, hoar crag, with toilsome hand;
From point to point the unwieldy ruin tossed,
Smokes down the steep, and grinds the cliffs to dust;
High bounding, sinking headlong, seeks the plain,
Cleaves the torn ground, and plows the foaming main:
Far plunge the crashing pines; the wild rocks roar,
Hurled with tumultuous fury to the shore;
Wide-rolling dust the neighboring concave fills,
And a long* swelling roar runs murmuring round the hills.
So down the bank, tremendous Jabin's car
Urged the pale throng, and drove the sounding war:
His foes plunged headlong in the crimson wave,
And chiefs, and warriors, found a liquid grave.
While thus in dreadful fight the hosts engaged,
The tumults thickened, and the clamours raged;
From Joshua's terrors Hazor's sons withdrew,
And distant from the shore their front renew.
With hideous strength, their ridgy lines ascend;
Red flame the shields; swords tremble; spears protend:
Pleased, the Chief views; too generous not to know,
And own, with praise, the merit of a foe.
From a tall rock he cast his flashing eyes,
And saw the varied scenes of combat rise.
While every foe bold Gibeon fiercely drove;
The tribes of Zimri backward slowly move:
Towered the high walls ascending volumes roll,
And clouds on clouds successive wrap the pole.
Greatly serene, he viewed the threatening doom,
Nor veiled his visage with a transient gloom;
But bade his chiefs, their bands for fight arrayed,
Lead on the war, and Hazor's host invade.
Then, where the fields displayed an easy course,
Along the shore he winged his rapid force;
Swift as a tempest down the bank he flies,
Cuts the red stream, and lifts tremendous cries --
Heavens! what dishonor pains this bleeding eye?
See, lost to shame, my friends, my heroes fly!
Turn, turn to triumph; swift to glory turn;
With generous shame let every bosom burn!
Shall your brave sires, that never knew to flee,
With pangs your flight, and tarnish'd honor, see;
And wish high Heaven had lent a milder doom,
And swept them childless to an earlier tomb?
Shall Dan, shall Asher, names of long renown,
Now lose the splendors of a deathless crown!
Forbid it Heaven! now wipe the hateful stain;
One bold exertion wins the immortal plain.
He spoke: at once, unfurled in glorious pride,
The sacred standard cast the view aside;
There Dan's bright eagle, high in pomp displayed,
Stretched his long wings, and reared his golden head;
Of gold his form in lucid triumph turned,
And streamy lightnings round him fiercely burned.
At once all Asher furious rushed to fight,
Each ardent warrior spurned inglorious flight.
With wider ruin heave the trembling fields;
Cars burst; cries roar* groans murmur; sound the shields.
As in some forest two red flames aspire,
And whelm huge pines in floods of surging fire,
Then swift through falling groves together driven
Roll over the mountain tops, and kindle heaven:
So, fierce and dreadful, front to front opposed,
Mid clouds of dust, the thundering squadrons closed:
Earth shakes; air rends; the trembling skies resound,
And night, and sad dismay, invade the embattled ground.
For war undaunted Hebron fiercely burned,
Nor even in Joshua's path to flight were turned.
Full on his sword they rushed, and bravely sell;
New bands with transport faced the slaughtering steel.
Incessant cries over all the combat rung;
Incessant spears through darkened either sung;
Swift flew the courser; swift the raging car:
Hoarse rose the tumult of the maddening war:
Less loud through forests winds impetuous roll,
The huge pines sink, and tempest rends the pole:
Less loud against Zembla mountain billows roar,
When the storm thunders on the frozen shore.
For Hebron's thousands Jabin's voice inspired,
And Joshua's deeds the sons of Israel fired.
Now where the Chief terrific swept the field,
And, clothed in terror, ranks on ranks repelled*
Whilst a red deluge over his footsteps spread,
And countless torrents spouted from the dead;
Swift to his path a chief of Asher ran,
Wild with dismay, and quivering thus began --
Wing, wing, thou best of men, thy friendly path --
Oh save the hero, or avenge his death! --
Now Zimri dies; from yon ascending ground,
I saw fierce Jabin point the fatal wound --
He spoke; at once, from all the Heathen train,
A voice of thunder heaved the affrighted plain:
Loud as hoarse whirlwinds torrent flames inspire,
When up the mountains rolls tempestuous fire;
Loud as the Almighty's voice, through either driven,
Pales the wide world, and shakes the walls of heaven;
Long shouts tremendous from the fields arise,
Burst over the hosts, and rend the clouded skies.
Through Israel's thousands thrills a dire alarm,
When thus great Joshua nerves each fainting arm --
Urge, my brave warriors, urge the glorious strife;
Wheel your red swords, and save the leader's life --
Shall Zimri die, whilst each astonished stands,
Nor sees these falchions useless in our hands?
Alive the fainting hero meets my sight;
And yet maintains the solitary sight --
He spoke, and furious wheeled his dreadful sword;
Back rolled the heathens; streams of slaughter poured:
Behind him Asher's host in deep array
Thronged darkening; clouds and death involved their way*
The bounding steeds bedewed their hoofs in blood,
And chiefs and monarchs swelled the purple flood.
Now, where bold Zimri braved the deathful ground,
O'erhung with foes, and pierced with many a wound,
Whilst laboring, panting, heaved his frequent breath,
And over his helmet flashed descending death;
Great Joshua, flaming, drove the embattled train;
Their lances flew, their falchions raged in vain.
Dire as a peal of thunder sweeps the skies,
He rushed, and Death sat frowning in his eyes:
For now brave Zimri scarce sustained the strife;
Sunk on one knee, and wished to sell his life.
Through the thick tumults of the broken war
Impetuous Jabin winged his rapid car;
With ruddy beams his lance uplifted shone;
His waving buckler mocked the sanguine sun;
'Twixt the bold chiefs, undaunted at the storm,
Sublime great Joshua reared his mighty form.
Now front to front the frowning heroes stood;
Their eyes red flames; their faces dropped with blood;
Their swords the lightning; two broad moons, their shields
Shot a fierce glory through the dreadful fields.
Then Jabin's heart, though formed of stubborn steel,
First shook with terror, and first learned to feel.
But roused by keen disdain, and vengeful ire,
Quick from his eye balls blazed infernal fire;
To earth, impatient, from the car he sprang;
His breast beat high; his rattling armor rang;
To die resolved, but as a king to die,
Like sudden thunder rose his bursting cry --
From this right hand receive, thou base-born slave,
A death too noble, but a dastard's grave;
Torn by the dogs, thy carcass here shall lie,
Or glut the fowls, that sweep the avenging sky.
The Chief disdained return. The Heathen's steel
Full on his helm with rapid fury fell,
Glanced by his sword, it clave the bloody ground;
Else had the Hero known no future wound.
Then with swift wheel, through Jabin's yielding side
Rushed his keen blade, and poured the sable tide;
Aghast, their monarch's fall his host beheld,
And sullen groans rung murmuring round the field.
Like Heaven's dread thunder Joshua raised his voice;
Hosts backward rolled, earth trembled at the noise --
On Gibeon's turrets stand thou still, O Sun!
Look down, thou Moon, on dreary Ajalon!
Fixed in high heaven the awful splendors stood,
And flamed tremendous on the field of blood;
From each dread orb ensanguin'd streams aspire,
The skies all mantling in fierce-waving fire;
Amazed, Canaan's realms the pomp descried;
The world grew pale; the hearts of nations died:
The bounding Hero seized the shining car,
Snatched the long reins, and shouted to the war:
Behind, fierce Asher swift to vengeance flew;
All dropped their spears, and all their falchions drew;
A sudden blaze gleam'd round the dusty gloom,
And plunged ten thousand warriors to the tomb.
For now, over all the fight, the heathens yield,
And Israel triumphs round the dreadful field.
High in the van, sublime great Joshua rode,
Winged the dire flight, and swelled the tide of blood;
Aghast, they see the lightning of his eyes,
And hear the thunders of his voice arise.
The plains are tumult all, convulsed affright,
Fierce ruin, wild amaze, and raging flight;
The Chariots stream; the steeds all eager bound,
Stretch over the plains, and sweep the rising ground;
Over rocks, over floods the thousands headlong fly,
And swords, and spears, and shields, behind them lie;
No stop, nor backward look, nor listening ear,
From plains to forests pants the full career;
Behind, the Hero wings his rapid way,
And dust and darkness shroud the beams of day.
So, borne in clouds of fire, an Angel's form
On impious Sodom drove the dreadful storm.
From heaven, in dreadful pomp, the Vision came;
Far, far behind him, streamed the angry flame;
The dark-red thunder, from his right hand hurled,
Upheav'd the sky, and fired the rocking world;
High over the storm, on wings of light, he rode,
And sailed, in lucid triumph, to the approving GOD.
Long rushed the victors over the sanguine field,
And scarce were Gibeon's loftiest spires beheld;
When up the west dark clouds began to rise,
Sailed over the hills, and lengthened round the skies.
A ridge of solding fire their summits shone;
But fearful blackness all beneath was thrown.
Swift round the sun the spreading gloom was hurled,
And night, and solitude, amazed the world.
At once the voice of deep-resounding gales
Rung slow, and solemn, in the distant vales;
Then through the groves, and over the extended plain,
With stormy rage the rapid whirlwinds ran:
Red over the glimmering hills, with pomp divine,
The lightning's flaming path began to shine;
Far round the immense unusual thunders driven,
Proclaimed the onset of approaching Heaven;
Astonished Nature owned the strange alarm,
And the world trembled at the impendent storm.
Over the dark fields aghast Canaan streamed;
Thick in their course the scattered bucklers gleam'd:
Behind them, Joshua urged the furious car,
And tenfo^d horrors hovered round the war.
But when the Chief the spreading storm surveyed,
And traced almighty arms in heaven displayed;
With piercing voice, he gave the great command --
Stand still, ye chosen sons, admiring stand!
Behold, what awful scenes in heaven arise!
Adore the power that brightens in the skies!
Now GOD's tremendous arm asserts his laws;
Now bids his thunder aid the righteous cause;
Unfolds how Virtue saves her chosen bands,
And points the vengeance doomed for guilty lands.
Behold, what flames shoot forth! what gloom ascends!
How nature trembles! how the concave rends!
How the clouds darken! see, in yonder sky,
Their opening skirts proclaim the Almighty nigh!
He spoke, and from the north a rushing sound
Rolled through the heavens, and shook the embattled ground:
At once a rapid path of dreadful flame
Burst from the skies, and poured a sanguine stream:
Throned on a dark red cloud, an Angel's form
Sailed awfully sublime, above the storm.
Half veiled in mist, his countenance, like a sun,
Inflamed the clouds, and through all either shone;
Long robes of crimson light behind him flowed;
His wings were flames; his locks were died in blood:
Ten thousand fiery shapes were round him driven,
And all the dazzling pomp of opening heaven.
Now, save Canaan's cries, that feebly rung,
Round the dark plain a horrid silence hung.
Stretched in dire terror over her quivering band,
The etherial Vision waved his sun-bright hand;
At once from opening skies red flames were hurled,
And thunders, rolled on thunders, rocked the world,
In one broad deluge sunk the avenging hail,
And, filled with tempest, roared the hoary vale;
The headlong whirlwinds boundless nature blend;
The streams rush backward; tottering mountains bend;
Down the tall steep their bursting summits roll,
And cliffs on cliffs, hoarse-crashing, rend the pole:
Far round the earth a wild drear horror reigns;
The high heavens heave, and sink the gloomy plains:
One sea of lightnings all the region fills:
Long waves of fire ride surging over the hills;
The nodding forests plunge in flame around,
And with huge caverns gapes the shuddering ground.
Swifter than rapid winds Canaan driven,
Refuse the conflict of embattled Heaven.
But the dire hail in vain the victims fly,
And death unbounded shook from all the sky;
The thunder's dark career; the Seraph's arm,
Fierce vengeance blazing down the immense of storm*
From falling groves to burning plains they flew;
Hail roars around, and angry blasts pursue;
From shaking heavens almighty arms are hurled,
And all the gloomy concave bursts upon the world.
No day like this the guilty earth had known;
Not Egypt's storm with equal terror shone*
No day like this over eastern hills shall rise,
Till Gabriel's trump inrolls the sinking skies.
For Heaven's dread stores, reserved for death, and war,
Fierce hail, and lightning, filled the rending air.
In vain the host attempted still to fly;
They fell, they rose again; but rose to die.
Mid thousand corses, there, beneath his shield,
Stalked a lone trembler through the sounding field:
Here, scattered wretches roam'd along the plain,
And sheltering bucklers hid their heads in vain.
On every si^e resistless foes engaged;
The lightning's livid blast around them raged;
While the shrill torrents of the avenging hail
Rushed on the pinions of the sweeping gale.
Rare, and more rare, were seen the sinking host,
'Till, whelmed beneath the deluge, all were lost.
Thus, when black midnight's terrors earth deform,
From the tall Andes bursts a blazing storm;
From steep to steep the ridgy flames aspire,
Bend over wide realms, and wrap the heavens in fire;
All nature trembles; tottering mountains rend;
Down the cliffs thunder; showers of fire descend;
Huge hills of ice, dissolved, and wastes of snow
Plunge in one deluge on the world below;
Over half Peru the floods tempestuous sweep,
And rocks, and groves, and towns, roll mingled to the deep.
The form began to move; the clouds gave way,
Their skirts all brightening with the crimson ray;
Far south, on wings of fire, the Angel flew,
And his clear splendors lessening left the view,
Down the broad regions of the midday skies,
Where glittering domes were seen, and scarcely seen to rise*
Through the long day, Canaan's widows stood,
And looked, all-anxious, toward the plain of blood;
Looked for the host, with victory's garlands crowned,
Enriched with spoils, and with fair fame renowned.
Their hands, to glad their friends with choice repast,
Culled every sweet, and wines of daintiest taste;
Often as a dusty cloud the whirlwinds reared,
In distant fields they thought their lords appeared:
Then, with new terrors, gazed, and gazed again,
'Till night, and sorrow darkened every plain.
The storm retired; the ensigns gave command,
And round their Leader thronged the conquering band.
Here sparkling eyes with joy and triumph burned;
Here pity silent from the slaughter turned;
Here for fallen friends the tear was seen to flow,
And sighs often spoke unutterable woe:
While Joshua's thoughts mount upward to the skies,
And fear, and wonder, in his bosom rise.
The stream, the walls they passed serenely slow,
Climbed the tall hills, and sought the plain below;
There crowned with flowers, their wives and children came
And songs rose grateful to the Eternal Name --
Blessed be the Power divine -- rejoiced they sung, --
The green vales echoed, and the forest rung --
Blessed be the hand, that clave the conscious sea,
And, robbed in thunder, swept our foes away!
Let endless blessings round our nation rise,
Cheer all our lives, and want us to the skies!
Thus strains of rapture charmed the listening gales,
While the low sunbeam glimmer'd on the vales:
To rest the camp retired: ten-thousand fires
Through the calm silence raised their bending spires:
The bright moon rose; winds cooled the cheerful even,
And wide magnificence enkindled heaven.
THE END.
